It has not been issued in His name, Exalted is He. If the ba is made transitive, it would be less far-fetched, for the meaning is: I have presented His name, Exalted, upon the intended object. If you say: How can the name be added to Allah, when Allah is the name, because the name and the named are one thing according to Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah? I say: It is said that 'name' here means naming, which is the utterance of the name, so the estimation is: By the remembrance of Allah I begin. And it is said that it is redundant, as in the saying: 'A caller calling him by the name of water,' meaning calling him by water. Then the estimation would be: By Allah I begin, and the mention of the name is to repel the suspicion of an oath. Allah: a name for the Essence that necessarily exists, deserving all praises, worshipped with right, having no derivation, and He is too great to have a derivation mentioned for Him. This is the choice of the Greatest Imam (Abu Hanifa) and al-Khalil, may Allah have mercy on them. The Creator alone is unique in it, not shared with anyone. He said: 'Do you know any equal to His name?' (Maryam 19:65) meaning: Do you know anyone named by this name other than Him. Its origin is 'ilah' (god), so the hamza was deleted contrary to analogy, and the definite article was substituted and became necessary, and it was stripped of the meaning of definiteness, and one of the two lams was assimilated into the other. Therefore it is said in the vocative: 'Ya Allah' with a cutoff, and it is said by analogy with a lightened hamza. Thus the assimilation and substitution are among the peculiarities of the majestic name, so that it is distinguished from others by the distinction of its named from others, with perfections not found in others. It is the most known of known things. Al-Rahman al-Rahim: two attributes derived from mercy. They differed whether they are the same meaning or different. Some said they are the same meaning, like nadman and nadim. Their meaning is 'possessor of mercy'; mentioning one after the other is for confirmation to reassure the hearts of the desirous, even though the first is not used except for the Creator. Al-Mubarrad said: It is bounty after bounty, and favor after favor. Some said there is a difference. Al-Rahman means generality: its meaning is the one who is compassionate to all His creation by providing for them in the world, not increasing the provision of the pious for their piety, nor decreasing the provision of the wicked for their wickedness. Al-Rahim means the one who rewards in the Hereafter, and forgiveness in the Hereafter is specific to the believers. Hence it is said in supplication: O Rahman of the world and the Hereafter. Thus in Ma'alim al-Tanzil. And in al-Kashshaf: In al-Rahman there is an intensity that is not in al-Rahim, i.e., because increased form usually indicates increased meaning, like 'qata'a' and 'qatta'a'. Thus, on this basis, the generality of al-Rahman is due to its not being specific to one of the two abodes, and the specificity of al-Rahim is due to its being specific to this world, contrary to what was mentioned in Ma'alim al-Tanzil, for there the generality of al-Rahman is due to its not being specific to some creatures (1) and they are the followers of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and Abu Mansur al-Maturidi. He said: 'A group of my ummah will continue to prevail over the truth, not harmed by those who oppose them, until the command of Allah comes while they are upon that.' The hadith was narrated by Muslim in the Book of Leadership, chapter: His statement: 'A group of my ummah will continue to prevail over the truth' (1920). (1) without some, and the specificity of al-Rahim is due to its being specific to some creatures, specifically the believers. And mercy: tenderness of heart, which is a psychological quality impossible for Him, Exalted. So it is either a transferred metaphor of beneficence, then it is an attribute of action, or of His will, then it is an attribute of essence. Or it is a representative metaphor: likening His action, Exalted, to the state of a king who is kind to his subjects, and he is tender to them, so he includes them in his good deeds, so the name is applied to him, and its ultimate meaning is intended: action or will, not its origin which is passion. So it is a representative metaphor. And the descriptive adjective is derived from 'rahima' while it is transitive, by making it intransitive, or by transferring it to a verb with damm. All this is based on the fact that al-Rahman is an attribute, and it is so originally, but it became a proper noun by predominance. Ibn Hisham said: The truth is the statement of al-A'lam and Ibn Malik that it is not an attribute but a proper noun. And it is built on its being a proper noun that in the basmalah and similar it is a substitute, not a modifier, and that al-Rahim after it is a modifier for it, not a modifier for the name of Allah, since the substitute does not precede the modifier, said by Shaykh al-Islam Zakariyya al-Ansari, and likewise said by the Imam al-Qadi al-Baydawi and Mulla Khusraw and in al-Durar. Al-Rahman al-Rahim: two names built for intensity. And Ibn al-Mubarak said: Al-Rahman: if asked, He gives; al-Rahim: if not asked, He becomes angry.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is a detailed linguistic and theological commentary on the basmalah. It begins by addressing the grammatical construction of 'Bismillah', discussing whether the ba is for transitivity. It then tackles the issue of whether 'ism' (name) and 'musamma' (named) are identical, affirming the Ahl al-Sunnah position that they are the same. The name 'Allah' is analyzed etymologically, emphasizing it has no derivation and is unique to the divine essence, a view attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa and al-Khalil. A Quranic verse (19:65) is cited to prove exclusivity. The derivation from 'ilah' is explained, with changes like hamza deletion and lam assimilation. The attributes al-Rahman and al-Rahim are then examined: whether they are synonymous or distinct. Two opinions are presented: one holds they are identical; another (from al-Kashshaf) distinguishes them by intensity and scope. The commentary favors that al-Rahman indicates universal mercy (general provision in this world) while al-Rahim indicates specific mercy (forgiveness in the Hereafter for believers). Mercy as a divine attribute is analyzed as metaphorically representing beneficence or will, not an emotional quality. Finally, it notes that al-Rahman has become a proper noun by predominance, supported by Ibn Hisham and others, affecting its grammatical role in the basmalah. The footnote mentions the Ahl al-Sunnah (Ash'ari and Maturidi) and a hadith on the steadfast group.

Key Terms
الرحمن (al-Rahman): An attribute of mercy with generality—encompassing all creation in this world through provision, regardless of faith.
الرحيم (al-Rahim): An attribute of mercy with specificity—particularly for believers in the Hereafter.
الرحمة (al-rahmah): Mercy; originally tenderness of heart, but when attributed to Allah it is a metaphor for His beneficence or will to do good.
بدل (badal): Grammatical substitute; in the basmalah, 'al-Rahman' is a substitute (badal) for 'Allah', not an adjective (na't).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because mercy is a created thing.
B) Because mercy as tenderness of heart is impossible for Allah, so it must refer to His beneficent action or will.
C) Because the word is not used in the Quran literally.
D) Because Allah does not actually have mercy.

Key Takeaway
Ar-Rahman denotes general mercy (this world), ar-Rahim denotes specific mercy (Hereafter for believers); mercy attributed to Allah is metaphorical for His action or will.

The Linguistic Definition of Al-Hamd and Its Conditions
Defines al-hamd linguistically with conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic definition of al-hamd, list its four conditions, and explain the distinction between fada'il and fawadil with examples.

Core Idea
Al-hamd is praise for a beautiful voluntary act, done with veneration, excluding ugliness and mockery.

This lesson unpacks the precise linguistic definition of al-hamd from the Hanafi commentary on Nur al-Idah. The definition includes key conditions that distinguish true praise from mere expression. Grasping these nuances is essential for understanding the full meaning of 'Al-hamdu lillah' and for correctly applying praise in Islamic contexts.

Guided Path
1
Extract the definition of hamd from the text
Identify the full linguistic definition: 'description/praise by the tongue, outwardly and inwardly, for a beautiful voluntary act that reaches the one praising or another, in a manner of veneration and preferment.'
The definition is broad, covering both outward and inward praise.
2
List the conditions of hamd
The definition contains four conditions: (1) the act must be beautiful (jamīl), (2) voluntary (ikhtiyārī), (3) the praise must reach the one praising or another (wāṣil), and (4) the praise must be with veneration and preferment (tabjīl wa tafḍīl).
Each condition excludes a specific counter-case: ugliness, compulsion, non-beneficial acts, and mockery.
3
Explain what each condition excludes
The condition 'beautiful' excludes ugly acts; 'voluntary' excludes compelled acts; 'reaching the praiser or another' ensures the act benefits someone; 'veneration and preferment' excludes mockery and sarcasm.
This ensures that hamd is genuine praise, not flattery or irony.
4
Distinguish between fada'il and fawadil
Fada'il (virtues) are intrinsic merits not dependent on others, like knowledge. Fawadil (favors) are transitive merits dependent on others, like benefaction. Hamd applies to both.
The author provides these examples to refute an objection that virtues are not transitive; they are transitive in effect.
5
Analyze the refutation of the objection
Some might argue that fada'il do not affect others, so hamd for them is different from hamd for fawadil. The author counters that virtues like knowledge have transitive effects (teaching), so both categories are similar.
Thus hamd covers all praiseworthy qualities, whether intrinsic or transitive.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحمد، جمع بينه وبين البسملة موافقة للتنزيل، وقدم البسملة عملاً بالكتاب والسنة والإجماع، لأن الأمة أجمعوا على كتابة البسملة في ابتداء الكتب والرسائل، قاله « القرطبي » في «جامعه»، ولعل سنده ما في الجعبري من قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، عن جبريل : ( إذا كتبتُم كتاباً فاكتبوا البسملة في أوله». فلذا ذكرنـــا بعـدهـا الحمد، والحمد هو في اللغة: الوصف، أي: الثناء باللسان ظاهراً وباطناً، على الفعل الجميل الاختياري، الواصل إلى الحامد أو غيره، على جهة التبجيل والتفضيل. فقيد بالجميل احترازاً عن القبيح، وبالتبجيل والتفضيل احترازاً عن الاستهزاء، سواء تعلق بالفضائل أم بالفواضل. والمراد بالفضائل المزايا الذاتية التي لا يتوقف تحققها على تعلقها بالغير، كالعلم والمراد بالفواضل المزايا المتعدية التي يتوقف تحققها على تعلقها بالغير كالأنعام. ومثلنا بالمثالين دفعاً للاعتراض الذي يقال في الفضائل، كما تتعدى بأثرها كذلك الفواضل فلا فرق فاندفع بذلك. وفي العرف: هو
Al-hamd: He combined it with the basmalah in accordance with the revelation, and he placed the basmalah first acting by the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus, because the ummah have agreed upon writing the basmalah at the beginning of books and letters. Al-Qurtubi said this in his Jami', and perhaps its chain is what is in al-Ja'buri from the Prophet, peace be upon him, from Jibril: 'When you write a book, write the basmalah at its beginning.' Therefore we mentioned al-hamd after it. And al-hamd in language is: the description, i.e., praise by the tongue, outwardly and inwardly, for a beautiful voluntary act that reaches the one praising or another, in a manner of veneration and preferment. So it is restricted to 'beautiful' to exclude what is ugly, and to 'veneration and preferment' to exclude mockery, whether it relates to virtues (fada'il) or favors (fawadil). By virtues are meant intrinsic merits whose realization does not depend on connection with others, like knowledge; by favors are meant transitive merits whose realization depends on connection with others, like benefaction. We gave two examples to repel the objection that might be raised concerning virtues, just as they are transitive in their effect, so too favors, so there is no difference, thus it is repelled. Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is a definition-ruling explaining the word 'al-hamd' (praise) as used in the phrase 'Al-hamdu lillah'. It begins by noting that the author combined the basmalah and hamd in the opening, following the Quranic pattern, and prioritized the basmalah based on the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus. A hadith from Jibril (via al-Ja'buri) is cited to support writing basmalah at the start of writings. The definition of hamd is then given: it is verbal praise (outward and inward) for a beautiful voluntary act that benefits the one praising or another, done with veneration (tabjil) and preferment (tafdil). This excludes praise for ugly acts or mockery. The praise applies to both 'fada'il' (intrinsic virtues like knowledge) and 'fawadil' (transitive favors like benefaction). The author explains the distinction between them and addresses an objection that virtues might not be transitive; he shows they are transitive in effect, so no distinction remains. The passage ends with 'In common usage: it is...' which is incomplete but indicates a customary definition.

Key Terms
الحمد (al-hamd): Linguistic definition: verbal praise for a beautiful voluntary act that benefits someone, done with veneration and preferment. Excludes ugliness and mockery.
الفضائل (al-fada'il): Intrinsic merits that do not depend on connection with others, such as knowledge.
الفواضل (al-fawadil): Transitive merits that depend on connection with others, such as benefaction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Al-hamd is praise for a beautiful voluntary act, with veneration and preferment, encompassing both intrinsic virtues and transitive favors.

Combining Salah and Salam in Blessings upon the Prophet
Author explains the ruling on combining salah and salam in salawat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining salah and salam when sending blessings upon the Prophet, identify the hadith evidence, and explain why including the family is recommended.

Core Idea
Combining salah and salam in blessings is more complete, though saying only one is not disliked.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah, a Hanafi commentary on Nur al-Idah, addresses the proper manner of sending blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him). While the primary focus is on linguistic analysis, the author also clarifies a key fiqh point: that the recommended (sunnah) practice is to combine both salah and salam, in obedience to the Quranic command and following prophetic guidance. Understanding this ruling helps students apply the correct adab in their daily salawat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage discusses sending blessings (salah) and peace (salam) upon the Prophet. Determine the hukm level: what does the author say about combining them?
The author states 'wa anna al-akmalu indana' – it is more complete in our school.
2
Locate the evidence (dalil)
The author cites two hadith: (1) 'Every speech that does not begin with blessing upon me is cut off...' (2) 'Whoever sends blessings upon me in a book...' Identify the type of dalil and its strength.
The hadith are ahad (zanni al-thubut) and their indication is also zanni.
3
Understand the Hanafi position on combining
Note that the author says combining is more complete, but it is not disliked to say only one. This implies the ruling is sunnah muakkadah, not wajib.
The hanafi_position_box confirms: sunnah muakkadah, mufta bihi is to say both.
4
Analyze the inclusion of the family (al)
The author explains that 'al' can mean followers, self, or household, and includes the family because salah without them is incomplete. This is based on a hadith: 'When you send blessings, include (them).'
Hanafi school emphasizes including family as part of the complete blessing.
5
Apply to daily practice
When reciting salawat, the student should combine salah and salam and include the family: 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad wa 'ala aali Muhammad...'
Common formula: 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad wa 'ala aali Muhammad wa sallim.'

(رب) العالمين، بتشديد الباء، وقد تخفف أي: متولي مصالح كل فرد من أفراد الموجودات بتبليغه الشيء حالة فحالة إلى كمال تربيته، ثم وصف به للمبالغة، كالعدل، فهو صفة من ربه يربه، فهو رب لحفظه ما يملكه، وهو : المالك والسيد والمصلح والمربي والمعبود، ولا يطلق على غيره تعالى إلا مقيداً، فلا يقال للمخلوق هو الرب معرفاً باللام، وإنما يقال له: رب الـدار والدابة، مع ، مضافاً، بمعنى . المالك للدار والدابة. ارجع إلى ربك، فالله رب العالمين). الألف واللام فيـه للتعريف، وعالمين جمع عالم، وهو في الأصل علم، ثم زيد فيه الألف للإشباع، كخـاتم، فعــالمين جمع عالم. وأُدخلت الألف واللام على الجمع، وهو اسم لما يعلم به، ثم غلب على ما سوى الله مـــن جوهر (۳) وعرض(۳)، وهي لإمكانها وافتقارها إلى مؤثر واجب لذاته، تدل على وجوب وجوده، فيكون مشتقاً من العلم - بفتح اللام بمعنى العلامة. وجمع مع أنه اسم جنس، لأنه أُريد به الأنواع والأفراد، ليشمل أجناسه المختلفة، أو لأنه يتوجه إلى عالم كل زمان، وكـان بـالـيـاء والـنــون جمع سالم، وهو لمن يعقل تغليباً للعقلاء، أو تقول: ساغ ذلك لمعنى الوصفيــة فـيـه، وهـي الدلالة علـى معنى العلم، وقيل: هو اسم وضع لذوي العلم من الإنس والملائكة والجن وتناول غيرهم بطريق التبع، فيكون مشتقاً من العلم بكسر العين، والفاعل بالفتح لم يجمع هذا الجمع إلا الـعـالـم والياسم، فيقال: الياسمين، والصفة قد خصت بالإضافة للعالمين، فجاز أن يكون نعتاً للجلالة أعرف المعارف، ولو تخالفا تعريفاً. ثم قولنا: الحمد لله رب العالمين فيه اقتباس لطيـف مـن القــرآن الكريم، والفرقان القديم، من غير إشعار بأنه منه، إذ هو شرط الاقتباس، حاول به افتتاح كتابه، ومن ثم جمع بينه وبين التسمية، رجاء حصول المقصود (والصلاة ) رحمة الله، وإفضاله له، وإنعامه

والسَّلامُ عَلَى سَيِّدِنَا مُحَمَّدٍ حَاتَم النَّبِيِّينَ، وَعَلَى آلِهِ.
وتعظيمه، بالألف مبدلة عن واو لفظاً، وبالواو كتابة، إلا إذا أضيف أو ثني، فقيل: صلاتك أو صلاتان، وقال « ابن درستويه»: لم يثبت بالواو في غير القرآن وهي: اسم من التصلية، أي: الثناء الكامل، ولما أن كان ليس في وسعنا سألناه من الله تعالى.
(و) كذا (السلام)، وهـو : اسم من التسليم، وقيل: مصدر ثلاثي أو مزيد، والأول أصح. والمعنى: جعله الله تعالى سالماً عن كل مكروه، وحيَّاه بما يليق بجلاله وعظمته لشريف الجناب، وجمعنا بينهما امتثالاً للأمر بهما ، وإن لم يكره إفراد أحدهما ، لأنه الأكمل عندنا، ولقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: كل كلام لا يبدأ فيه بالصلاة علي فهو أقطعُ ممحوقٌ مِنْ كلّ بركة ، وقوله : « مَنْ صَلَّى عَلَيَّ
في كتاب، لم تَزَلْ المَلائِكَةُ تستغفر له، ما دام اسمي في ذلك الكتاب» (۳). (عـلـى سـيـدنـا)، خبر للمعطوفين، وجاز أن تكون خبر الثاني، وخبر الأول محذوف عند سيبويه». وقيل: يجوز القلب. (محمد)، أشهر أسمائه الشريفة، وهي ألف اسم، وسمي بـه إلهامـاً، والمعنى: ذات كـثـر خـصالـه المحمودة، أو كثر الحمد له في الأرض والسماء، أو كثر حمده تعالى له (خاتم النبيين)، النبيء، بالهمز، من النبأ أي الخبر، وبلا همز، وهو الأكثر من النبوة، وهي الرفعة، لأن النبي مرفوع الرتبة، فمن الأول يكون فعيلاً بمعنى مُفْعِل، يعني: منبئ الأخبـار والـغـيـوب عــن الله تعالى، ولمـا كـانت الصلاة عليه غير تامة بدون الصلاة على الآل كما في شرح التأويلات»، عطفها. فقال: (وعلى آله). بألف مبدلة عن الهمزة المبدلة عن الهاء عند البصريين، وعن الواو عند الكوفيين، والأول أصح لغة. وإضافة الآل إلى الضمير قليلة، أو غير جائزة، والمختار الآل والأحسن آل محمد، ولكنه أضاف إليه اختصاراً، والآل يطلق فبالاشتراك اللفظي على ثلاثة معان، أحدها: الجند والأتباع، نحو آل فرعــــون. والثاني: النفس، نحو: آل موسى وآل هارون يعني : نفسهما، والثالث بمعنى أهل البيت خاصة، نحو: آل محمد . وإنما وجب ذكر آله أيضاً في الصلاة معه لقوله : ( إِذا صَلَّيتُمْ فَعَمِّمُوا » .
(۱) وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿ يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا صَلُّوا عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمُوا تَسْلِيماً ) [ الأحزاب: ٥٦ ]. (۲) ذكره الطرابلسي في الكشف الإلهي (٦٦٠/١)، والعجلوني في كشف الخفاء (١٥٦/٢). (۳) أخرجه الطبراني في الأوسط (۲۳۲/۲)، والعجلوني في كشف الخفاء (۳۳۸/۲). (٤) ذكره القاري في المصنوع (۲۷/۱)، والسخاوي في المقاصد الحسنة (٦٧/١)، وقال: ويمكن أن يكون بمعنى حديث «صلوا علي وعلى أنبياء الله، فإن الله بعثهم كما بعثني وقال العجلوني في كشف الخفاء (۹۲/۱): وقيل المعنى إذا صليتم علي فأدخلوا معي آلي وأصحابي.
- ۲۳ -
Lord of the worlds, and prayer. (2) If my gratitude for the blessing of Allah is a blessing from Him, then for such a thing gratitude is obligatory, so how can I attain gratitude except by His grace, even if days are long and life continues? And mentioning the bestowal of favor after indicating the merit of the essence in some expressions is a reminder of the realization of two merits for Allah. (Rab) of the worlds, with shaddah on the ba, and it may be lightened, meaning: the one who manages the interests of every individual of existent things by conveying to them thing by thing until the perfection of their nurturing, then it is used as an attribute for exaggeration, like al-adl. So it is an attribute from rabba yarubbu, so He is a lord because of His preservation of what He possesses. And He is the owner, master, reformer, nurturer, and worshipped. And it is not applied to other than Him, exalted is He, except restrictedly. So it is not said of a creature that he is 'ar-rabb' with the definite article, but rather it is said to him: rabb ad-dar (lord of the house) and rabb ad-dabbah (lord of the animal), as an addition, meaning the owner of the house and animal. Return to your Lord, so Allah is the Lord of the worlds. The alif and lam in it are for definition, and 'alamin is the plural of 'alam, which originally meant a sign (alam), then alif was added for fullness, like khatam, so 'alamin is the plural of 'alam. And the definite article was added to the plural, and it is a name for that by which something is known, then it became predominant for everything other than Allah from substance and accident, and they, due to their possibility and need for an effect necessarily existent in itself, indicate the necessity of His existence. So it is derived from 'alam – with fatha on the lam, meaning sign. And it is pluralized even though it is a generic noun, because it is intended for species and individuals, to include its different types, or because it is directed to the world of every time. And it was with ya and nun, a sound plural, and it is for those who possess intellect, as a predominance of the rational, or it is permissible due to the adjectival meaning in it, which is the indication of the meaning of knowledge. And it is said: it is a name placed for those possessing knowledge from humans, angels, and jinn, and includes others by way of following, so it is derived from 'ilm with kasra on the 'ayn, and the active participle with fatha is not pluralized in this way except al-'alam and al-yasm, so it is said: al-yasamin. And the adjective is particularized by addition to al-'alamin, so it is permissible for it to be an attribute for the Majesty, the most definite of definite nouns, even if they differ in definition. Then our saying: al-hamdu lillahi rabbil 'alamin contains a subtle quotation from the Noble Qur'an and the Ancient Criterion, without indicating that it is from it, for that is the condition of quotation. He attempted by it to open his book, and thus he combined it with the basmalah, hoping for the attainment of the intended goal. (And prayer) mercy of Allah, His favor upon him, and His grace. And peace be upon our master Muhammad, the seal of the prophets, and upon his family. And glorification of him, with alif substituted for waw in pronunciation, and with waw in writing, except when it is added or dualized, so it is said: salatuka or salatan. Ibn Durustawayh said: It is not established with waw outside of the Qur'an. And it is a noun from tasliyah, i.e., perfect praise. And since it is not within our capacity, we ask it from Allah Almighty. (And) likewise (peace), and it is a noun from taslim, and it is said: a triliteral or augmentative infinitive, and the first is more correct. And the meaning: may Allah make him safe from every disliked thing, and greet him with what befits His majesty and grandeur for the noble station. And we combined them both in obedience to the command regarding them, although it is not disliked to single out one of them, because it is the more complete in our view, and due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Every speech that does not begin with blessing upon me is cut off, devoid of all blessing,' and his saying: 'Whoever sends blessings upon me in a book, the angels will continue to ask forgiveness for him as long as my name is in that book.' (Upon our master) is the predicate of the conjoined elements, and it is permissible for it to be the predicate of the second, and the predicate of the first is omitted according to Sibawayh, and it is said: inversion is permissible. (Muhammad): the most famous of his noble names, and they are a thousand names, and he was named by it through inspiration. And the meaning: with many praiseworthy attributes, or much praise for him on earth and in heaven, or much praise from Allah for him. (Seal of the prophets): an-nabi', with hamzah, from an-naba' meaning news, and without hamzah, and that is more common, from nubuwwah meaning highness, because the prophet is of elevated rank. So according to the first, it is fa'il in the sense of muf'il, meaning: one who informs of news and unseen things from Allah Almighty. And since prayer upon him is not complete without prayer upon the family, as in Sharh at-Ta'wilat, he conjoined it, so he said: (And upon his family), with alif substituted for the hamzah which is substituted for the ha according to the Basrans, and for the waw according to the Kufans, and the first is more correct linguistically. And adding 'al' to the pronoun is rare or not permissible, and the chosen form is 'al' and the best is 'al Muhammad', but he added it to the pronoun for brevity. And 'al' is applied by homonymy to three meanings: one: army and followers, like 'al Fir'awn'; second: self, like 'al Musa and al Harun' meaning themselves; third: specifically the household, like 'al Muhammad'. And it is necessary to mention his family along with him in prayer because of his saying: 'When you send blessings, include (them).'
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This is a front matter passage from Imdad al-Fattah, a commentary on Nur al-Idah. The author opens with the hamdalah (praise of Allah) and salawat upon the Prophet (peace be upon him). In the first part, he explains the meaning of 'Rabb al-'Alamin', breaking down the word 'Rabb' as the owner, master, and nurturer, and 'Alamin' as the plural of 'Alam' (sign), referring to all creation, especially rational beings. He notes that the phrase is a subtle quote from the Quran, used to open the book with blessing. In the second part, he discusses 'al-salah' and 'al-salam', explaining that 'salah' means perfect praise and mercy from Allah, while 'salam' means safety from all evil. He combines them in obedience to the Quranic command, and states that although saying only one is not disliked, the more complete is to say both. He also cites hadiths about the virtue of beginning speech with salawat. Then he explains the name 'Muhammad', meaning praised abundantly, and 'Khatam an-Nabiyyin' (Seal of the Prophets), deriving 'nabi' from either news or high rank. Finally, he comments on 'Alihi' (his family), noting that 'Al' has three meanings: followers, self, and household. The Hanafi school holds that including the family in salawat is necessary for completeness, based on the command to send blessings on the Prophet and his family. This passage demonstrates the author's method: combining linguistic analysis with legal and theological points.

Key Terms
صلاة (Salah): Mercy and favor from Allah, or perfect praise (thana' kamil) when from creatures.
سلام (Salam): Safety from every disliked thing; a greeting of honor.
آل (Al): Family or household; can mean followers, self, or specifically the Prophet's household.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on combining salah and salam when sending blessings on the Prophet in the Hanafi school?
A) It is wajib to combine both.
B) It is permissible but the more complete is to say both.
C) It is disliked to combine them.
D) It is only recommended to say salah alone.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school regards combining salah and salam in blessings upon the Prophet, along with his family, as the more complete form (sunnah muakkadah), though saying only one is not disliked.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Author's Introduction and Methodology in Nur al-Idah
Author explains his lineage, methodology, and reason for writing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the author's purpose, explain his methodological principle of relying on ahl al-tarjih, and distinguish between iltimas, amr, and du'a.

Core Idea
Nur al-Idah is a concise beginner's guide on ibadat, compiled only from rulings confirmed by ahl al-tarjih.

This passage is the author's preface to his commentary 'Imdad al-Fattah' on his own work 'Nur al-Idah'. Here, al-Shurunbulali explains his lineage, the meaning of certain key terms, and his strict methodology: he includes only what the later verifiers (ahl al-tarjih) have deemed sound, avoids unnecessary debate, and aims to make scattered issues from lengthy books accessible to beginners. Understanding this preface helps you appreciate the reliability and structure of the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his full name
Read the opening lines to find the author's name, his nickname (Abu al-Ikhlas), his lineage (al-Shurunbulali), and his madhhab (Hanafi). Recognize that his full name is Hasan ibn Ammar ibn Ali ibn Yusuf al-Wafai al-Shurunbulali al-Hanafi.
The author is a Hanafi scholar from the 17th century CE.
2
Understand the specific meaning of 'al' (آل)
The author explains that the term 'al' (family) is restricted to nobles and followers of prophets, not commoners. For example, 'Al al-Nabi' refers to the believers, and 'Al Fir'awn' is used because Pharaoh was regarded as noble.
This is a linguistic clarification relevant to the salutation in the text.
3
Distinguish between iltimas, amr, and du'a
The author defines iltimas as a request from an equal, amr as a command from a superior to an inferior, and du'a as a supplication from an inferior to a superior. This appears in the explanation of 'iltamasa' (he requested).
This distinction is useful in understanding the nature of the request made to him.
4
Grasp the author's purpose for writing
The author states that some friends asked him to compose an introduction on acts of worship (ibadat) that would gather for the beginner what is scattered in lengthy books. He responded for the sake of reward and named his work 'Nur al-Idah and Najaat al-Arwah'.
The book is intended as a concise, beginner-friendly compilation.
5
Note the author's criteria for inclusion
He only mentions what ahl al-tarjih (scholars of preponderance) have confirmed as sahih. He avoids verbosity and unnecessary debate, but includes proofs from Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma' as needed. He also mentions that if he includes an unsound opinion, he will alert the reader.
This methodology ensures reliability and focus for the beginner.

الطَّاهِرينَ، وَصَحَابَتِهِ أَجْمَعِينَ. قَالَ العَبْدُ الفَقِيرُ إلَى مَوْلاهُ الغَنِي، أبو الإخلاص حَسَنُ الوَفَانِي الشرنبلالي الحنفي.
وأراد بالتعميم التعميم على الآل. قاله العلامة «شهاب الدين النقشبندي». وهـو مخصوص بالأشراف وألي الخطر والشأن. فلا يقال: آل الإسكاف والحايك، فيقال: آل العباس، ولـمـا تـصـور فرعون بصورة الأشراف قيل: آل فرعون وآل النبي هم: المؤمنون؛ لأن آل الأنبياء متبعوهم، كذا في منهاج الضوء ». ( الطاهرين) عن الأدناس كلها، حسية ومعنوية، وفيـه بـرـاعة الاستهلال). (وصحابته أجمعين)، تأكيد، وهو جمع أجمع، وإن كان صفة في الأصل اسم تفضيل، فإن قولنا: ا قرأت الكتاب أجمع معناه: أتم جمعاً في قراءتي من كل شيء، نقل إلى معنى الجمع. (قال الـعـبـد) الذليل، ( الفقير، إلى مولاه الغني الجليل عن كل شيء، إذ هو موجد الكائنات، وهي المفتقرة إليه بأسرها. (أبو الإخلاص كنيتـه مـن سـاداتنا بني الوفاء، أعاد الله علينـا مـن بـركـاتـهم ومددهـم، وشهرتهم وظهور كراماتهم تغني عن ذكر ألقابهم أدام الله تنزيل البركات، والفيض والنفحات بأنفاسهم، وسر أسلافهم على المسلمين، خصوصاً وفاء النيل) السعيد بمحروسة مصــر، لدفــع الضرر والإصر ) عن المخلوقات، لإيجاد الرزق بالزرع، وحصول الأقوات بدوام الأوقات (حسن) بن عمار بن علي بن يوسف ( الوفائي) () ، طريقة ( الشرنبلالي)، بلداً (الحنفي) مذهباً، النسبة إلى فَعِيْلة فَعِلي، وإلى فَعِيليَّة فعِيلي وعلى هذا قيل: الدين حنيفي والمذهب حنفــي وقــال عـلـيـه الـصـلاة والسلام: « بُعِثْتُ بالحَنِيفيَّةِ السَّمْحَةِ » ، أي: بالملة الحنيفية، والإمام الأعظم – أبو حنيفة- حنيفي غير حنفي، ومتبع أبي حنيفة حنيفي وحنفي، والإمام الشافعي له الله ) بعه حنيفي غير حنفي.
إِنَّهُ التَمَسَ مِنِّي بَعْضُ الأَخِلاءِ - عَامَلَنَا اللهُ وَإِيَّاهُمْ بِلُطْفِهِ الْخَفِيّ - أَنْ أَعْمَلَ مُقَدِّمَةٌ فِي العِبَادَاتِ عَلَى المُبْتَدِي مَا تَشَتَّتَ مِنَ الْمَسَائِلِ فِي الْمُطَوَّلاتِ، فَاسْتَعَنْتُ بِاللَّهِ تَعَالَى، وَأَجَبْتُهُ طَالِباً للثوَابِ، ولا أذكُرُ إِلا مَا جَزَمَ بِصِحْتِهِ أَهْلُ التَّرْجِيْحِ، مِنْ غَيْرِ إطْنَابِ، وَسَمَّيْتُهُ: «دُورَ الإِيضَاحِ، وَنَجَاةَ الأَرْوَاحِ ) .
( إنه التمس) الالتماس طلب المساوي، والأمر : طلب الأعلى ممـن دونــه، والدعــاء: طلـب الأسفل من الأعلى ( مني بعض الأخلاء) يعني: المتحابين في الله، رحمه الله، (عاملنا الله وإياهم بلطفه الخفي)، وكرمه وإحسانه، ( أن أعمل)، أي: أجمع من كلام أئمتنا (مقدمة)، مـن قـدم اللازم بمعنى تقدم، لا من قدم المعتدي (في) مسائل ( العبادات) على صفة ( تقرب على المبتدي) بسهولة ألفاظها وظهور معانيها، وتذكر المنتهي لغزارة نقلها، ما تشتت عن موطنه، ومظنة وجدانــه ( من المسائل) المهمات المذكورة (في) الكتب ( المطولات)، إذ قد لا يصل إليها الطالب إلا بتعب شديد، ولا يقف العالم بها عليها إلا بعد أمد، وإن لم يكن غيـر بـعـيـد، (فاستعنت بالله تعالى)، إذ لا قوة لي، وفوضت إليه أمري وما خاب من إلى عزته التجأ، بل أعزه ونصره، ومـن يتوكل على الله، فهو حسبه، إن الله بالغ أمره. (وأجبته ) بجميع ما أراد، طالباً للثواب) لقول رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: ( إِذَا مَاتَ ابنُ آدمَ، انْقَطَعَ عَمَلُهُ إِلا مِنْ ثَلاثٍ، صَدقةٍ جَارية، أو عِلْمٍ يُنْتَفَعُ بِهِ، أَو وَلَدٍ صَالِحٍ يَدْعُو لَهُ ) ( حديث صحيح أخرجه مسلم. ولا أذكر ) في هذا الجمع ( إلا مـا جـزم بصحته) وترجيحه (أهل) التصحيح و الترجيح)، وذكرت في شرحه بيان وجهه، وإن كان مقابلاً بقول مرجح فهو أيضاً صحيح، وإذا ذكرت غير الصحيح فأنبه عليه، وأثبته لفائدة العلم بـه، لمـا يقتضيه المقام. وأخليت هذا الشرح المبارك عن طريقة الجدل قصداً، وعن سياق مذهب المخالف إلا نزراً)، وذكرت أدلة المسائل من الكتاب والسنة والإجماع، بقدر الحاجة والإمكان ( مـن غـيـر إطناب)، أطنب الرجل: أتى بالبلاغة في الوصف مدحاً كان أو ذماً، كذا في « القاموس». انتهى. وفي الاصطلاح أن يكون اللفظ زائداً على المعنى وسميته : ( نور الإيضاح»)، إذ العـلـم نـور ( « ونجاة الأرواح » ( إذ لا نجاة إلا بالعلم، قال أبو الدرداء الله : « كُنْ عَالِمَاً، أو مُتَعَلِّمَاً، أو مُسْتَمَعَاً، ولا تكن الرابع فتهلك». وإذا أشرنا إلى فضل العلم، فلنذكر شيئاً مما يدل عـلـى فضله، وفضـل أهـلـه،
The pure ones, and all his companions. The poor servant in need of his Rich Master, Abu al-Ikhlas Hasan al-Wafani al-Shurunbulali al-Hanafi said. And he intended by generalization the generalization over the family. The scholar Shihab al-Din al-Naqshbandi said it. And it is specific to nobles and people of danger and status. So it is not said: the family of the shoemaker and the weaver, but it is said: the family of al-Abbas. And when Pharaoh was portrayed in the image of nobles, it was said: the family of Pharaoh. And the family of the Prophet are the believers; because the family of the prophets are their followers, as in Minhaj al-Daw'. (The pure) from all impurities, sensory and spiritual, and in it is the excellence of the beginning. (And all his companions), an emphasis, and it is the plural of ajma', although it was originally an adjective, a superlative noun. For our saying: I read the book entirely (ajma') means: I completed a complete collection in my reading of everything, transferred to the meaning of collection. (The slave said) the humiliated, (the poor) to his Rich Master, Exalted above everything, for He is the Creator of all beings, and they are all in need of Him. (Abu al-Ikhlas is his nickname from our masters the Banu al-Wafa', may Allah renew upon us from their blessings and their supports, and their fame and the manifestation of their miracles suffice from mentioning their titles. May Allah perpetuate the descent of blessings, and the emanation and breaths through their breaths, and the secret of their predecessors upon the Muslims, especially Wafa' al-Nil) the happy in guarded Egypt, to repel harm and burden from the created beings, to provide sustenance through farming, and the attainment of provisions by the continuity of times. (Hasan) bin Ammar bin Ali bin Yusuf (al-Wafai) ( ), method (al-Shurunbulali), as a town, (al-Hanafi) as a madhhab. The attribution to fa'ilah is fa'li, and to fa'iliyyah is fa'ili, and upon this it is said: the religion is hanifi and the madhhab is hanafi. And the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'I was sent with the easy hanifiyyah', i.e., the hanifi religion. And the Greatest Imam – Abu Hanifa – is hanifi, not hanafi, and the follower of Abu Hanifa is hanifi and hanafi, and Imam al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, is hanifi, not hanafi. Indeed, some friends asked me – may Allah treat us and them with His subtle kindness – that I compose an introduction on acts of worship that would bring together for the beginner what is scattered from the issues in the lengthy books. So I sought help from Allah Almighty, and I answered him seeking reward. And I only mention what the people of tarjih (preponderance) have confirmed as sound, without verbosity. And I named it: 'Nur al-Idah (The Light of Clarification) and Najaat al-Arwah (Salvation of Souls).' (Indeed, he requested) iltimas is a request from an equal, and amr (command) is a request from a superior to an inferior, and du'a' (supplication) is a request from an inferior to a superior. (From me some friends) meaning those who love each other in Allah, may Allah have mercy on him. (May Allah treat us and them with His subtle kindness), and His generosity and goodness. (That I compose) i.e., compile from the speech of our imams (an introduction) from the necessary qadama meaning to precede, not from the transitive qadama. (On) issues (of acts of worship) in a manner (that draws near to the beginner) by the ease of its wording and clarity of its meanings, and reminds the advanced due to the abundance of its transmission, (what has become scattered from its place and locus) (from the important issues mentioned) (in) the books (the lengthy ones), because the student may not reach them except with great difficulty, and the scholar may not come upon them except after a long time, even if not far. (So I sought help from Allah Almighty), for I have no power, and I entrusted my affair to Him. And whoever relies on Allah, He is sufficient for him; indeed, Allah will accomplish His purpose. (And I answered him) with all that he wanted, seeking reward, because of the saying of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him: 'When a son of Adam dies, his deeds cease except from three: ongoing charity, beneficial knowledge, or a righteous child who prays for him' – a authentic hadith narrated by Muslim. (And I do not mention) in this compilation (except what the people of correction and tarjih have confirmed as sound). And I mentioned in its commentary the explanation of its reasoning, and even if it is faced by a preponderant opinion, it is also sound. And if I mention what is not sound, I will alert to it and record it for the benefit of knowing it, as the context requires. And I emptied this blessed commentary from the method of argumentation intentionally, and from the context of the opposing madhhab except a little. And I mentioned the proofs of the issues from the Book, the Sunnah, and Ijma', to the extent of need and possibility, without verbosity. (Verbosity means) a man described with excellence in description, whether praise or blame, as in al-Qamus. End. And in terminology it means that the wording exceeds the meaning. And I named it: (Nur al-Idah), because knowledge is light, (and Najaat al-Arwah), because there is no salvation except through knowledge. Abu al-Darda', may Allah be pleased with him, said: 'Be a scholar, or a student, or a listener, and do not be the fourth, lest you perish.' And since we have indicated the virtue of knowledge, let us mention something that indicates its virtue and the virtue of its people.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction (muqaddimah) to his commentary 'Imdad al-Fattah' on 'Nur al-Idah'. The author, Hasan al-Shurunbulali al-Hanafi, begins by praising Allah and sending blessings on the Prophet and his companions. He then introduces himself with his full name and lineage, explaining the meanings of 'al' (family) and how it is specifically used for noble lineages, such as the family of the Prophet (the believers) or the family of Abbas. He clarifies the difference between 'hanifi' (pertaining to the religion of hanifiyyah) and 'hanafi' (pertaining to the madhhab of Abu Hanifa). On page 26, he states that some friends requested him to compile a concise book on acts of worship (ibadat) that gathers issues scattered in lengthy works, making it accessible for beginners. He responded for the sake of reward, naming his work 'Nur al-Idah and Najaat al-Arwah'. He emphasizes that he only includes relied-upon positions (what ahl al-tarjih have deemed saheeh) and avoids unnecessary debate, though he includes proofs from Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma' as needed. He also highlights the importance of knowledge, quoting the hadith about deeds ceasing after death except for three, and the saying of Abu al-Darda' about being a scholar or student.

Key Terms
آل (al): Family or household, specifically used for noble persons or followers of a prophet. In this text, it is restricted to nobles (ashraf) and significant figures, not commoners.
التماس (iltimas): A request or solicitation from an equal, as opposed to amr (command from superior) or du'a (supplication from inferior).
المطولات (al-mutawwalat): The lengthy, comprehensive legal works from which the author gathered scattered issues for his concise book.
أهل الترجيح (ahl al-tarjih): The scholars who determine the stronger, relied-upon opinion among conflicting legal positions. The author restricts his work to what they have confirmed as sahih.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary purpose of the book 'Nur al-Idah' according to the author?
A) To present a detailed analysis of all fiqh rulings with proofs
B) To compile a concise introduction on acts of worship for beginners, gathering scattered issues from lengthy books
C) To refute the opinions of other madhhabs in detail
D) To provide a commentary on the entire Quran

Key Takeaway
Al-Shurunbulali wrote Nur al-Idah to provide beginners with a concise, reliable summary of ibadat rulings, drawing only on positions verified by ahl al-tarjih.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Author's Introduction and the Hanafi Definition of Fiqh
Author's introduction with methodology and definition of fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the author's criteria for including rulings in Nur al-Idah and explain the Hanafi definition of fiqh.

Core Idea
A reliable fiqh text relies on established madhhab positions, not personal opinion.

The author, Imam al-Shurunbulali, begins his work 'Nur al-Idah' by explaining why he wrote it and how he selected its content. He emphasizes that he only includes rulings that have been affirmed as sahih (sound) and rajih (preponderant) by the scholars of tarjih within the Hanafi school. He then defines fiqh according to Imam Abu Hanifa and cites numerous proofs on the virtue of knowledge. This lesson unpacks the author's methodology and the core definition of fiqh that underpins the entire text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the request and response
The author received a request from some brothers to compile a primer on acts of worship. He responded by writing this book. Note the distinction between iltimas (request among equals) and amr/du'a.
2
Understand the author's selection criteria
The author states he only includes what the ahl al-tarjih have affirmed as correct. This means he relies on the preponderant positions within the Hanafi school, not his own opinion or rare narrations.
This ensures the book is a reliable reference for the madhhab.
3
Know the Hanafi definition of fiqh
Imam Abu Hanifa defined fiqh as 'the soul's knowledge of what is for it and against it' specifically concerning actions (amalan). This distinguishes fiqh from theology (kalam) and spirituality (tasawwuf).
Fiqh is about practical rulings, not beliefs or inner states.
4
Recognize the virtue of knowledge proofs
The author cites Quranic verses and hadith, such as 'Whoever Allah intends good for, He gives him understanding of religion' and 'The scholars are the heirs of the prophets.' These establish the high status of fiqh and its pursuit.
These proofs are meant to motivate the student.

وقال أبو حنيفة في تعريف الفقه: « إنه معرفة النفس ما لها وما عليها. يعني عملاً، إذ معـرفـة مـا لهـا ومـا عـلـيـهـا مـن الاعتقاديات علم الكلام، ومعرفة ما لها وما عليها من الوجدانيات علم التصوف والأخلاق، ومعرفة ما لها وما عليها عملاً، من العمليات هي: الفقه المصطلح عليه، وكذا قال «فخـر الإسلام البزدوي»: إن الفقه علم المشروع بصفة الإتقان والعمل به ومن الآيات قوله تعالى: شَهِدَ اللَّهُ أَنَّهُ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ وَالْمَلَيْكَةُ وَأُولُوا الْعِلْمِ قَابِمَا بِالْقِسْطِ [ العمران : ١٨]. بدأ بنفسه سبحانه وتعالى، وثنى بملائكته، وثلـث بـأهل العلم. وقوله تعالى: ﴿يَرْفَعِ اللَّهُ الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا مِنكُمْ وَالَّذِينَ أُوتُوا الْعِلْمَ دَرَحَتْ) [المعادلة : ١١] مــن « التاتارخانيـــة». وقـــال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «فضل العَالِمِ على العَابِدِ بِسَبْعِينَ درجَةً، مَا بينَ كُلِّ دَرَجتينِ كَمَا بينَ السَّمَاءِ وَالْأَرْضِ». أخرجه عبد الرزاق في ( الجامع . قاله الشيخ أبو الحسن البكري». وفي « التاتارخانيـة قـال ابـن عباس : « للعلماءِ دَرَجَاتٌ فوق المؤمنين بسبعمائة درجة، ما بينَ كُلِّ درجتين مسيرة خمسمائة عام ). وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَقُل رَّبِّ زِدْنِي عِلْمًا [ظلة: ١١٤]. ومن الحديث قوله : ( مَنْ يُرِدِ اللَّهُ بِهِ خيراً، يُفَقَهُ فِي الدين ، وقوله : ( العلماء ورثة الأنبياء. ومعلوم أن لا رتبة فوق رتبة النبوة، ولا شرف فوق شرف الوراثة من الأنبياء، وقوله : ( الإيمان عريان، ولباسه التقوى، وزينته الحياه وثمرته العلم . وقوله : مَا عُبِدَ اللهُ بِشيءٍ أَفضَلَ مِنْ فقه في دين، ولفقيه واحدٌ أشدُّ على الشيطان من ألف عابد، ولـكــل شـيء عماد، وعماد هذا الدِّينِ الفقه ). وقوله : ( خير دينكم أيسره، وأفضلُ العبادة الفقه» . ومن الآثار،
Indeed, some brothers - may Allah treat us and them with His hidden grace - asked me to compose a preface in [the subject of] acts of worship, gathering for the beginner what is scattered of the issues in the lengthy books. So I sought help from Allah Most High, and answered him, seeking reward. And I mention only what the people of tarjih have affirmed as correct, without prolixity. And I named it 'Nur al-Idah wa Najat al-Arwah'... (then explanation of terms) ... The meaning of knowledge is clear to the intellect, for it is in reality a psychological perception. Abu Hanifa defined fiqh as 'the soul's knowledge of what is for it and against it' meaning concerning actions... and he quoted verses and hadith on the virtue of knowledge.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction (muqaddimah) to his book 'Nur al-Idah'. He begins by stating that some friends requested him to compile a primer on acts of worship (ibadat) that collects scattered issues from longer works in a manner accessible to beginners. He emphasizes that he only includes rulings affirmed by the scholars of tarjih (preponderance) and avoids verbosity. The book's title means 'Light of Clarification and Salvation of Souls'. He then explains key terms: 'iltimas' (request from an equal), 'amr' (command from superior to inferior), 'du'a' (supplication from inferior to superior), and the meaning of 'mukhtasar' (concise work). He cites the hadith about deeds ceasing except for three, indicating his hope for continuing reward. He states his methodology: only mention sahih and rajih positions, note if a weak report is included for benefit, avoid dialectical argumentation, and provide proofs from Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma as needed. He then transitions to the virtue of knowledge (ilm) and fiqh. He defines knowledge as 'psychological perception' (idrak nafsani). He gives Abu Hanifa's definition of fiqh: 'the soul's knowledge of what is for it and against it' with respect to actions (amalan), distinguishing it from kalam (theology) and tasawwuf (spiritual states). He also quotes Fakhr al-Islam al-Pazdawi's definition. Numerous Quranic verses and hadith are cited extolling the virtue of scholars and knowledge, including the famous hadith 'Whoever Allah intends good for, He gives him understanding of religion' (man yuridillahu bihi khairan yufaqqihu fiddin). This sets the stage for the legal content that follows.

Key Terms
التماس (iltimas): A request made to an equal, as opposed to 'amr' (command to a subordinate) and 'du'a' (supplication to a superior).
المقدمة (muqaddimah): An introductory section that precedes the main subject; from 'qadama' meaning to precede.
المطولات (mutawwalat): Extended, lengthy books (i.e., comprehensive works of fiqh).
نور الإيضاح (Nur al-Idah): The title of the book, meaning 'Light of Clarification' - science is light.
الفقه (fiqh): Knowledge of the soul of what is for it and against it, with respect to actions (amalan); the science of practical rulings derived from detailed evidence.
أهل الترجيح (ahl al-tarjih): The scholars who weigh evidence and determine the strongest (rajih) positions within the madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's introduction, what is the primary criterion for including a ruling in this book?
A) The ruling must be from the Qur'an or Sunnah only.
B) The ruling must be affirmed as sahih (correct) and rajih (preponderant) by the scholars of tarjih.
C) The ruling must be the personal view of the author.
D) The ruling must be from the later fatwa collections.

Key Takeaway
The author's introduction establishes that Nur al-Idah contains only the preponderant Hanafi rulings and defines fiqh as the knowledge of practical actions (amaliyyah).

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
10 min
Defining Fiqh in the Hanafi School
Defining fiqh and distinguishing it from other sciences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of fiqh and distinguish it from kalam and tasawwuf.

Core Idea
Fiqh is practical knowledge of what the soul must do and avoid.

Before diving into legal rulings, we must understand what fiqh itself means. The great Hanafi imams, Abu Hanifa and al-Bazdawi, gave precise definitions that set fiqh apart from theology and spirituality. This lesson unpacks those definitions and their implications.

Guided Path
1
Understand the threefold division of knowledge
The text divides knowledge into three categories: beliefs (kalam), inner states (tasawwuf/ethics), and actions (fiqh). Identify which category each belongs to and note their subjects.
This division is critical to avoid conflating fiqh with other Islamic sciences.
2
Grasp Abu Hanifa's definition
Read Abu Hanifa's definition: 'It is the soul's knowledge of what is for it and against it, meaning practically.' Understand that 'practically' (عملا) excludes theoretical belief and inner state purification, focusing solely on outward actions.
The phrase 'what is for it and against it' covers both rights (malal) and duties (malayha).
3
Examine al-Bazdawi's complement
Al-Bazdawi adds: 'Fiqh is knowledge of the legislated with mastery and action.' Note the emphasis on mastery (al-itqan) and action (al-amal), reinforcing that fiqh is not mere memorisation but applied understanding.
This aligns with the practical orientation of the entire Hanafi school.
4
Recognise the practical focus
The passage explicitly states that fiqh is about 'actions' (al-‘amaliyyat). Contrast this with kalam (beliefs) and tasawwuf (spiritual states), which are separate disciplines. Fiqh governs what we do, not what we believe or feel.
This distinction guides the scope of fiqh studies.

And what they have of reward, and we mention its definition: Indeed its meaning is clear to the intellect, for it is in reality a psychological perception, because everyone who has this perception has knowledge insofar as he has perception, and whoever does not, does not. Abu Hanifa said in defining fiqh: 'It is the soul's knowledge of what is for it and against it' meaning practically, because knowledge of what is for it and against it in matters of belief is the science of kalam, and knowledge of what is for it and against it in spiritual states is the science of tasawwuf and ethics, and knowledge of what is for it and against it practically, from actions, is the conventional fiqh. Likewise, Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi said: 'Fiqh is the knowledge of the legislated with the quality of mastery and acting upon it.' And from the verses is the saying of Allah Most High: 'Allah witnesses that there is no deity except Him, and the angels and those of knowledge, standing firm in justice' [Al-Imran: 18]. He began with Himself, and seconded with His angels, and thirded with the people of knowledge. And His saying: 'Allah will raise those who have believed among you and those who have been given knowledge by degrees' [Al-Mujadila: 11]. From al-Tatarkhaniyya. And the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The superiority of the scholar over the worshiper is seventy degrees, between each two degrees is like the distance between heaven and earth.' Narrated by Abd al-Razzaq in al-Jami'. Said by al-Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Bakri. And in al-Tatarkhaniyya, Ibn Abbas said: 'Scholars have degrees above the believers of seven hundred degrees, between each two degrees is a distance of five hundred years.' And His saying: 'And say, my Lord, increase me in knowledge' [Taha: 114]. And from the hadith is his saying: 'Whoever Allah wishes good for, He gives him understanding of the religion.' And his saying: 'The scholars are the heirs of the prophets.' And it is known that there is no rank above the rank of prophethood, nor honor above the honor of inheritance from the prophets. And his saying: 'Faith is naked, its garment is piety, its adornment is modesty, and its fruit is knowledge.' And his saying: 'Allah was not worshiped with anything better than understanding in religion, and one faqih is more severe against Satan than a thousand worshipers, and everything has a pillar, and the pillar of this religion is understanding.' And his saying: 'The best of your religion is the easiest, and the best of worship is understanding.' And from the athar: (footnotes)...
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a front matter section from Imdad al-Fattah, a commentary on Nur al-Idah, establishing the virtue of knowledge (especially fiqh) and defining fiqh as a discipline. The author begins by clarifying that true knowledge is a psychological perception, then presents Abu Hanifa's definition of fiqh: 'the soul's knowledge of what is for it and against it' – meaning practical knowledge (al-‘amal), as distinct from theology (kalam) and spirituality (tasawwuf). Abu Hanifa divides knowledge into three categories: beliefs (kalam), inner states (tasawwuf), and actions (fiqh). The term fiqh in its technical sense refers only to the third. Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi adds that fiqh is 'knowledge of the legislated with mastery and action.' Then the author cites Quranic verses on the virtue of knowledge (3:18, 58:11, 20:114) and multiple hadith, including the famous one that the scholar's rank is seventy degrees above the worshiper, and that scholars are heirs of the prophets. He quotes sayings of Ibn Abbas, Imam Ali, Abu al-Aswad, and Fath al-Mawsili on the excellence of knowledge. Finally, he gives a practical fiqh example: the wound caused by a trained hunting dog is considered like the sharpness of a civilized tool, making the hunt lawful, due to the dog's knowledge – contrasting with an untrained dog. This example illustrates how knowledge (here, the dog's training) affects legal rulings. The passage is a collection of proofs (dalil naqli) from Quran, hadith, and sayings of early scholars to motivate the study of fiqh.

Key Terms
الفقه (al-fiqh): According to Abu Hanifa: 'معرفة النفس ما لها وما عليها عملاً' – the soul's knowledge of its rights and duties practically. According to al-Bazdawi: 'علم المشروع بصفة الإتقان والعمل به' – knowledge of the legislated with mastery and action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does Abu Hanifa mean by the phrase 'عملاً' in his definition of fiqh?
A) That fiqh is theoretical knowledge
B) That fiqh is only about inner states
C) That fiqh concerns practical actions, not beliefs or spiritual states
D) That fiqh is the same as kalam

Key Takeaway
Fiqh in the Hanafi school is the practical, action-oriented knowledge of Shariah rulings, distinct from theology and spirituality.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
15 min
The Virtue of Knowledge and the Rank of the Scholar
Extolling the virtue of knowledge and citing proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to cite the primary Quranic verses and hadith on the virtue of knowledge and explain their significance for the study of fiqh.

Core Idea
Scholars are the heirs of the prophets; their rank is above worshipers.

The study of fiqh is not merely an intellectual exercise; it is a highly meritorious act. This lesson gathers the Quranic verses, hadith, and sayings that elevate the scholar’s status and show how knowledge, even in a trained animal, can affect legal rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic proofs
Read the verses: 3:18 (Allah, angels, and people of knowledge bear witness), 58:11 (Allah raises those with knowledge), and 20:114 (prayer for increase in knowledge). Note how each highlights the exalted position of knowledge.
Verse 3:18 begins with Allah Himself, then angels, then scholars – showing their proximity to the divine.
2
Understand the hadith on scholars’ superiority
Analyse the hadith: 'The superiority of the scholar over the worshiper is seventy degrees...' and 'Scholars are the heirs of the prophets.' Recognise that these establish the immense virtue of acquiring knowledge, especially fiqh.
The hadith contrasting scholar and worshiper shows that knowledge combined with action is superior to mere worship without knowledge.
3
Reflect on the sayings of early authorities
Read the statements of Ibn Abbas, Ali, Abu al-Aswad, and Fath al-Mawsili. They reinforce the theme: knowledge guards you, knowledge is better than wealth, scholars are kings over kings, and the heart dies without knowledge.
These sayings provide moral and spiritual motivation for the student.
4
Apply the example of the trained dog
The passage gives a practical fiqh example: the wound of a trained dog (الكلب المعلم) is treated like that of a tool, making the hunted animal lawful. This is because of the dog's knowledge (training). Contrast with an untrained dog, whose wound is not lawful. See how knowledge (training) changes the ruling.
This example illustrates that the virtue of knowledge extends to animals, showing its universal impact on legal rulings.

وما لهم من الثواب، ونذكر تعريفه فنقول: إن معناه واضح عند العقل، إذ هو بالحقيقة إدراك نفساني، لأن كل من وجد له هذا الإدراك، وجد له العلم من حيث أنه وجد الإدراك، ومن لا فلا. وقال أبو حنيفة في تعريف الفقه: « إنه معرفة النفس ما لها وما عليها. يعني عملاً، إذ معرفة ما لها وما عليها من الاعتقاديات علم الكلام، ومعرفة ما لها وما عليها من الوجدانيات علم التصوف والأخلاق، ومعرفة ما لها وما عليها عملاً، من العمليات هي: الفقه المصطلح عليه، وكذا قال «فخر الإسلام البزدوي»: إن الفقه علم المشروع بصفة الإتقان والعمل به ومن الآيات قوله تعالى: شَهِدَ اللَّهُ أَنَّهُ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ وَالْمَلَيْكَةُ وَأُولُوا الْعِلْمِ قَابِمَا بِالْقِسْطِ [ العمران : ١٨]. بدأ بنفسه سبحانه وتعالى، وثنى بملائكته، وثلث بـأهل العلم. وقوله تعالى: ﴿يَرْفَعِ اللَّهُ الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا مِنكُمْ وَالَّذِينَ أُوتُوا الْعِلْمَ دَرَحَتْ) [المعادلة : ١١] مــن « التاتارخانيـــة». وقـــال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «فضل العَالِمِ على العَابِدِ بِسَبْعِينَ درجَةً، مَا بينَ كُلِّ دَرَجتينِ كَمَا بينَ السَّمَاءِ وَالْأَرْضِ». أخرجه عبد الرزاق في ( الجامع . قاله الشيخ أبو الحسن البكري». وفي « التاتارخانيـة قـال ابـن عباس : « للعلماءِ دَرَجَاتٌ فوق المؤمنين بسبعمائة درجة، ما بينَ كُلِّ درجتين مسيرة خمسمائة عام ). وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَقُل رَّبِّ زِدْنِي عِلْمًا [ظلة: ١١٤]. ومن الحديث قوله : ( مَنْ يُرِدِ اللَّهُ بِهِ خيراً، يُفَقَهُ فِي الدين ، وقوله : ( العلماء ورثة الأنبياء. ومعلوم أن لا رتبة فوق رتبة النبوة، ولا شرف فوق شرف الوراثة من الأنبياء، وقوله : ( الإيمان عريان، ولباسه التقوى، وزينته الحياه وثمرته العلم . وقوله : مَا عُبِدَ اللهُ بِشيءٍ أَفضَلَ مِنْ فقه في دين، ولفقيه واحدٌ أشدُّ على الشيطان من ألف عابد، ولـكــل شـيء عماد، وعماد هذا الدِّينِ الفقه ). وقوله : ( خير دينكم أيسره، وأفضلُ العبادة الفقه» . ومن الآثار،
(۱) أخرجه أبو يعلى في مسنده (١٦٣/٢)، والديلمي في مسند الفردوس (۱۲۸/۳).
(۲) لم أهتد إليه في كتب الحديث فيما بين يدي، ولكن ذكره ابن قدامة المقدسي في مختصر منهاج القاصدين (۱۳).
(۳) أخرجه البخاري في العلم، باب: ( من يرد الله به خيراً يفقهه في الدين (۷۱)، ومسلم في الزكاة، باب النهي عن المسألة (۱۰۳۷).
(٤) أخرجه أبو داود في العلم (٣٦٤١) ، وابن ماجه في المقدمة، باب فضل العلماء والحث على طلب العلم (۲۲۳).
(٥) أخرجه الديلمي في مسند الفردوس (۱۱۲/۱)، والصغاني في الموضوعات (۳۱/۱).
(٦) أخرجه الترمذي في نوادر الأصول (۱۳۵/۱)، والطبراني في الأوسط (١٩٤/٦).
(۷) الحديث مركب من حديثين الشطر الأول أخرجه أحمد في مسنده (٤٧٩/٣)، والشطر الثاني أخرجه الترمذي في نوادر الأصول (١٣٥/١).

قال الإمام علي : « العِلْمُ خيرٌ مِنَ المالِ العلم يحرسك، وأنت تحرس المال، والعلم حاكم، والمال محكوم عليه ، وقال أبو الأسود ( ليس شيء أعزُّ مِنَ العلم، الملوك حكام على الناس، والعلماء حكام على الملوكِ». انتهى. من ( التاتارخانية». وقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: « العــالم سلطان الله في الأرضِ، فَمَنْ وَقَعَ فِيهِ فَقَدْ هَلَكَ » ). أخرجه الديلمي، قاله الشيخ « أبو الحسن البكـــري». وفي « التاتارخانية». وقال ابن عباس : ( خير سليمان بن داود بينَ العِلْمِ والمَالِ والمُلكِ فَاخْتَارَ العِلْمَ، فأعطي المال والملك معه (۳). ومن كلام الحكماء، قال بعضهم: ليت شعري، أي شيء أدرك من فاته العلم؟ وأي شيء فاته من أدرك العلم؟. ومن كلام العارفين، قال «فتح الموصلي»: أليس المريض إذا منع الطعام والشراب والدواء يموت؟ قالوا: نعم، قال: كذلك القلب، إذا منع عنـه الحكمة والعلم ثلاثة أيام يموت. ومن مسائل الفقه: إلحاق جرح الكلب المعلم ونحوه، وكـل جارح بدرجة إباحة المذكي اختياراً بواسطة علمه، بخلاف الكلب الجاهل، فإن الله تعالى أحل صيد الجارحة النجسة المعلمة لفضل علمها. ومن الأخبار التي وردت في فضل العلماء قوله : يستغفر للعلماء ما في السمواتِ والأرض ) ) . وأي منصب أعلى من منصب من يشتغل ملائكة السماء والأرض بالاستغفار له؟ وقوله : ( موتُ قبيلة أيسر مِنْ مَوتِ عَالِم . وقال : ( مَنْ همَّهُ، وَرَزَقَهُ مِنْ حَيثُ لا يَحْتَسِبُ ) ) . وقال : « أوحى الله عز وجل إلى إبراهيم عليه الصلاة والسلام: إني عليمٌ أحب كل عليم . و قال : « فَضْلُ العَالِمِ عَلَى العَابِدِ، كَفَضْلِي عَلَى أَدْنَى رَجُلٍ مِنْ أَصْحَابِي ) .
تَفَقَّة في دين
الله، كَفَاهُ الله

(۲) أخرجه الديلمي في مسند الفردوس (١٤٩/٤).

(۳) لم أهتد إليه فيما بين يدي من كتب الحديث، وإنما ذكره القرطبي في تفسيره (۳۰۰/۱۷).
(٤) أخرجه أبو داود في العلم باب الحث على طلب العلم (٣٦٤١) ، وابن ماجه في المقدمة، باب: فضل العلماء والحث على طلب العلم (۲۲۳).
(0) أخرجه البيهقي في شعب الإيمان (٢٦٤/٢) ، والديلمي في مسند الفردوس (١٤٩/٤).
(٦) ذكره السيوطي في ذيل اللآلئ المصنوعة (۳۳/۱) ، وابن عراق في تنزيه الشريعة (۲۷۱/۱).
(۷) ذكره الحافظ العراقي في تخريج أحاديث الإحياء في كتاب العلم، البال الأول (۸) وقال: ذكره ابن عبـد الـبـر تعليقاً ولم أظفر له بإسناد.
(۸) أخرجه الترمذي في العلم باب ما جاء في فضل الفقه على العبادة (٢٦٨٥)، والدارمي في المقدمة (۲۸۹).
And what they have of reward, and we mention its definition: Indeed its meaning is clear to the intellect, for it is in reality a psychological perception, because everyone who has this perception has knowledge insofar as he has perception, and whoever does not, does not. Abu Hanifa said in defining fiqh: 'It is the soul's knowledge of what is for it and against it' meaning practically, because knowledge of what is for it and against it in matters of belief is the science of kalam, and knowledge of what is for it and against it in spiritual states is the science of tasawwuf and ethics, and knowledge of what is for it and against it practically, from actions, is the conventional fiqh. Likewise, Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi said: 'Fiqh is the knowledge of the legislated with the quality of mastery and acting upon it.' And from the verses is the saying of Allah Most High: 'Allah witnesses that there is no deity except Him, and the angels and those of knowledge, standing firm in justice' [Al-Imran: 18]. He began with Himself, and seconded with His angels, and thirded with the people of knowledge. And His saying: 'Allah will raise those who have believed among you and those who have been given knowledge by degrees' [Al-Mujadila: 11]. From al-Tatarkhaniyya. And the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The superiority of the scholar over the worshiper is seventy degrees, between each two degrees is like the distance between heaven and earth.' Narrated by Abd al-Razzaq in al-Jami'. Said by al-Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Bakri. And in al-Tatarkhaniyya, Ibn Abbas said: 'Scholars have degrees above the believers of seven hundred degrees, between each two degrees is a distance of five hundred years.' And His saying: 'And say, my Lord, increase me in knowledge' [Taha: 114]. And from the hadith is his saying: 'Whoever Allah wishes good for, He gives him understanding of the religion.' And his saying: 'The scholars are the heirs of the prophets.' And it is known that there is no rank above the rank of prophethood, nor honor above the honor of inheritance from the prophets. And his saying: 'Faith is naked, its garment is piety, its adornment is modesty, and its fruit is knowledge.' And his saying: 'Allah was not worshiped with anything better than understanding in religion, and one faqih is more severe against Satan than a thousand worshipers, and everything has a pillar, and the pillar of this religion is understanding.' And his saying: 'The best of your religion is the easiest, and the best of worship is understanding.' And from the athar: (footnotes)...
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a front matter section from Imdad al-Fattah, a commentary on Nur al-Idah, establishing the virtue of knowledge (especially fiqh) and defining fiqh as a discipline. The author begins by clarifying that true knowledge is a psychological perception, then presents Abu Hanifa's definition of fiqh: 'the soul's knowledge of what is for it and against it' – meaning practical knowledge (al-‘amal), as distinct from theology (kalam) and spirituality (tasawwuf). Abu Hanifa divides knowledge into three categories: beliefs (kalam), inner states (tasawwuf), and actions (fiqh). The term fiqh in its technical sense refers only to the third. Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi adds that fiqh is 'knowledge of the legislated with mastery and action.' Then the author cites Quranic verses on the virtue of knowledge (3:18, 58:11, 20:114) and multiple hadith, including the famous one that the scholar's rank is seventy degrees above the worshiper, and that scholars are heirs of the prophets. He quotes sayings of Ibn Abbas, Imam Ali, Abu al-Aswad, and Fath al-Mawsili on the excellence of knowledge. Finally, he gives a practical fiqh example: the wound caused by a trained hunting dog is considered like the sharpness of a civilized tool, making the hunt lawful, due to the dog's knowledge – contrasting with an untrained dog. This example illustrates how knowledge (here, the dog's training) affects legal rulings. The passage is a collection of proofs (dalil naqli) from Quran, hadith, and sayings of early scholars to motivate the study of fiqh.

Key Terms
العالم (al-alim): A person of knowledge, especially religious knowledge (fiqh).
العابد (al-abid): A person devoted to worship (e.g., prayer, fasting) without necessarily possessing deep knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what makes a hunting dog's wound equivalent to a sharp tool, making the hunted animal halal?
A) The dog's breed
B) The dog's training (knowledge)
C) The dog's size
D) The hunter's intention

Key Takeaway
Knowledge, especially fiqh, is immensely virtuous in the Shariah, elevating the scholar above the mere worshiper and even affecting legal rulings on permissibility of hunted animals.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Exalted Status of Scholars: Proofs from Qur'an and Sunnah
Compilation of hadith on virtue of knowledge and scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state at least four hadith that demonstrate the virtue of scholars and explain why the Hanafi madhhab considers the pursuit of fiqh as the highest form of worship.

Core Idea
Scholars are the inheritors of prophets; their rank surpasses even martyrs on the Day of Judgment.

This passage from the beginning of a classical Hanafi fiqh text serves as a spiritual foundation. The author gathers narrations to inspire the student to approach the study of fiqh with reverence and understanding. Recognizing the lofty status of scholars motivates the seeker to embody the adab (etiquette) of learning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall purpose
Understand that this passage is front matter intended to motivate the student by highlighting the immense virtue of knowledge and scholars in Islam.
Such prefaces are common in Hanafi fiqh works; they establish a sacred tone.
2
Extract key hadith on virtue
From the passage, pick out at least four prophetic narrations that explicitly praise 'ilm and 'ulama. Examples: 'The superiority of the scholar over the worshiper is like my superiority over the lowest man' and 'The death of a tribe is easier than the death of a scholar.'
Note the chains quoted (e.g., al-Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud) to appreciate authenticity.
3
Relate 'ilm to action
Observe how the passage links knowledge with divine acceptance and forgiveness, not mere accumulation. The hadith 'Allah says: I did not place My knowledge in you to punish you' emphasizes that knowledge demands practice.
Hanafi fiqh stresses that knowledge without action is blameworthy.
4
Analyze the fiqh example
The passage uses the ruling on trained dogs (jawarih mu'allamah) to show that knowledge affects legal permissibility. A trained dog's hunting is allowed because of its 'knowledge', contrasting with an untrained one.
This illustrates how the virtue of knowledge even applies to animals, reinforcing the theme.
5
Reflect on the promised reward
The lengthy hadith describing a magnificent city beneath the Throne for scholars is meant to inspire diligence. Contemplate how this reward correlates with the effort of learning and teaching fiqh.
Such descriptions are common in targhib (motivational) narrations.
