(۷) ذكره الحافظ العراقي في تخريج أحاديث الإحياء في كتاب العلم، الباب الأول (۸) وقال: ذكره ابن عبـد الـبـر تعليقاً ولم أظفر له بإسناد. (۸) أخرجه الترمذي في العلم باب ما جاء في فضل الفقه على العبادة (٢٦٨٥)، والدارمي في المقدمة (۲۸۹).
وقال : فَضْلُ العَالِم عَلَى العَابِدِ، كَفَضْلِ القَمَرِ ليلةَ البدرِ عَلَى سَائِرِ الكواكب ). وقال : يشفع يوم القيامةِ ثلاثة: الأنبياء، ثم العلماء، ثم الشهداء ) (). فأعظم بمرتبة هي تلو النبوة، وفـوق الشهادة، مع ما ورد في فضل الشهادة، وقال : ( مَنْ أَحَبَّ أنْ ينظر إلى عتقاءِ اللهِ مِنَ النَّارِ، فَلينظر إلى العُلَمَاءِ والمُتَعَلِّمِينَ ) (۳). وقال : ( خمس مِنَ النَّظَر عِبَادَةُ: النظر إلى الأبوين عبادة، والنظر في المصحفِ عبادة، والنظر إلى الكعبة عِبَادَةٌ، والنظرُ في زَمْزَمَ عِبادةٌ ، يحط الخطايـا حـطـا، والنظر إلى العالم عبادة » . وقال : ( مَنْ أكرمَ عَالِماً فَقَدْ أكرم سبعينَ نَبياً، ومَنْ أكرمَ متعلماً فقد أكرَمَ سبعينَ شهيداً، ومَنْ أَحَبَّ العِلْمَ والعُلَمَاءَ لا تُكْتَبُ عليهِ خَطِيئَةٌ أيامَ حَيَاتِهِ » . وقال : ( يَبْعَثُ اللَّهُ العباد يوم القيامةِ، ثُمَّ يميزُ العُلماء، فيقولُ: يا معشر العلماء، إني لم أضَعْ فِيكُمْ عِلْمِي إِلا لِعِلْمِي بِكُمْ، فَلَمْ أَضَعْ عِلْمِي فِيكُمْ لأعذبكُم، انطلقوا فقدْ غَفَرْتُ لَكُمْ . ثم قال عليه الصلاة والسلام: يقول الله تعالى لا تحقِرُوا عبدَاً لي آتِيتُهُ عِلْماً، فإني لم أحقره حين علمته . وعن مجاهد عن (E) (1) (V) عائشة ، أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «سألت جبريل عليه الصلاة والسلام عن ثواب العلماء، فقال: يـا محمد، إنَّ لله تعالى مدينةً تحت العرش من مسك أذفر لها جنات وأنهار، في جوفها سبعون ألف بيت من جوهر واحد، طول كل بيت ألف فرسخ، وعرضه مثل ذلك، في كل بيت ألف زاوية، في كـلّ زاوية ألف سرير، ومن السرير إلى السرير ألف ذراع، وعلى كل سرير ألف فراش، فــوق كــل فـراش ألف حوراء مِنَ الحور العين، وعلى كل واحدة ألف حلة، لا تواري حـلـة حـلـة، ولا يــاري الـحـلـل الجلد، ولا يواري الجلد اللحم، ولا يواري اللحم العظم، ولا يواري العظم المخ، يرى بعضـه مـن بعض، كما ترى السلكة في الياقوتة البيضاء، وعلى كل واحدة منهنَّ ثلاثة آلاف ذؤابة من المسكِ (1) أخرجه الترمذي في العلم، باب ما جاء في فضل الفقه على العبادة (۲۶۸۲) وأبو داود في العلـم، بـاب الحـث على طلب العلم (٣٦٤١). (۲) أخرجه ابن ماجه في الفتن، باب ذكر الشفاعة (٤۳۱۳)، والبيهقي في شعب الإيمان (۱۷۰۷). (۳) ذكره العجلوني في كشف الخفاء (۲۲۲/۲)، وقال: قال ابن حجر نقلاً عن السيوطي: كذب موضوع. (٤) الحديث مركب من عدة أحاديث بعضه أخرجه السيوطي في الجامع الصغير (٣٩٦٦)، وبعضه الديلمي في مسند الفردوس (٢٩٧/٤) وبعضه المناوي في الفيض القدير (٢٩٩/٦). (٥) ذكره ابن الجوزي في العلل المتناهية (۱۰۷/۱)، والديلمي في مسند الفردوس (٥٧٦/٣) مختصراً. (٦) أخرجه الطبراني في الأوسط (٣٠٢/٤). (۷) أخرجه البيهقي في المدخل إلى السنن الكبرى (٣٤٤/١) ، وابن عدي في الكامل (١١١/٤). -YA-
Imam Ali said: 'Knowledge is better than wealth; knowledge protects you, whereas you protect wealth; knowledge is a ruler, wealth is ruled.' And Abu al-Aswad said: 'Nothing is more precious than knowledge; kings rule over people, and scholars rule over kings.' End. From al-Tatarkhaniyyah. And the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'The scholar is the authority of Allah on earth; whoever falls into him has perished.' Al-Daylami narrated it; Sheikh Abu al-Hasan al-Bakri said it. And in al-Tatarkhaniyyah: Ibn Abbas said: 'Sulayman ibn Dawud was given the choice between knowledge, wealth, and dominion; he chose knowledge, and was given wealth and dominion along with it.' From the words of the wise: Some said: 'O that I knew what has been attained by one who missed knowledge? And what has been missed by one who attained knowledge?' From the words of the gnostics: Fath al-Mawsili said: 'Does not the sick person, if deprived of food, drink, and medicine, die?' They said: 'Yes.' He said: 'Similarly the heart, if wisdom and knowledge are withheld from it for three days, dies.' Among the fiqh issues: The attachment of the wound caused by a trained dog and the like, and every predator, to the degree of permissibility of the slaughtered animal by choice due to its knowledge, contrary to the ignorant dog, for Allah has permitted the hunting of the impure predator when trained, for the virtue of its knowledge. Among the reports regarding the virtue of scholars is His saying: 'The inhabitants of the heavens and the earth seek forgiveness for the scholars.' And what station is higher than the station of one for whom the angels of heaven and earth are engaged in seeking forgiveness? And His saying: 'The death of a tribe is easier than the death of a scholar.' And He said: 'Whoever's concern is [religion], Allah will suffice him with provision from whence he does not expect.' And He said: 'Allah revealed to Ibrahim: I am Knowing, and I love every knower.' And He said: 'The superiority of the scholar over the worshiper is like my superiority over the lowest man among my companions.' (And in the hadith:) 'Whoever acquires understanding in the religion of Allah, Allah suffices him.' (Narrated by al-Baghdadi, Ibn al-Jawzi, etc.) And He said: 'The superiority of the scholar over the worshiper is like the superiority of the full moon over the rest of the stars.' And He said: 'On the Day of Resurrection, three intercede: the prophets, then the scholars, then the martyrs.' So how great is a rank that follows prophethood and surpasses martyrdom, despite what has been reported about the virtue of martyrdom! And He said: 'Whoever loves to look at the freed slaves of Allah from the Fire, let him look at the scholars and the students.' And He said: 'Five kinds of looking are worship: looking at one's parents is worship, looking in the Quran is worship, looking at the Ka'bah is worship, looking at Zamzam is worship (it erases sins completely), and looking at the scholar is worship.' And He said: 'Whoever honors a scholar has honored seventy prophets; whoever honors a student has honored seventy martyrs; and whoever loves knowledge and scholars will not have a sin recorded against him during his life.' And He said: 'Allah will raise the servants on the Day of Resurrection, then He will distinguish the scholars and say: O assembly of scholars, I did not place My knowledge in you except out of My knowledge of you; I did not place My knowledge in you to punish you. Go forth, for I have forgiven you.' Then he ﷺ said: 'Allah says: Do not belittle a servant of Mine to whom I have given knowledge, for I did not belittle him when I taught him.' And from Mujahid from A'ishah that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'I asked Jibril about the reward of the scholars. He said: O Muhammad, Allah has a city beneath the Throne made of musk and ambergris; it has gardens and rivers, within it are seventy thousand houses of one jewel, the length of each house is a thousand parasangs and its width is similar; in each house are a thousand corners, in each corner a thousand couches, between each couch is a thousand cubits; on each couch are a thousand beds, on each bed a thousand maidens from the houris; on each maiden are a thousand garments, one garment not covering the next, nor do the garments cover the skin, nor does the skin cover the flesh, nor does the flesh cover the bone, nor does the bone cover the marrow; each is seen through the other, as a thread is seen in a white sapphire; and on each of them are three thousand locks of musk.' (Narrated by al-Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud, etc.)
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of narrations and sayings extolling the virtues of knowledge and scholars, typical of the introductory material (khutbah or preface) in classical Hanafi fiqh works. The author, al-Sharnublali or later commentators, gathered these texts to motivate the reader and emphasize the great merit of seeking Islamic knowledge. The passage includes statements from Ali ibn Abi Talib, Abu al-Aswad, Ibn Abbas, and a variety of prophetic hadith, often with chains of transmission. It also mentions a quote from Fath al-Mawsili comparing withholding knowledge from the heart to depriving a sick person of food and medicine. The author then brings a fiqh example: the permissibility of eating game caught by a trained dog as opposed to an untrained one, linking it to the virtue of knowledge even in animals. The bulk of the passage is hadith describing the high status of scholars, their intercession on the Day of Judgment, and the immense reward prepared for them in Paradise. The inclusion of these narrations serves to inspire the student to pursue fiqh with sincerity and reverence. As a front_matter passage, it does not establish legal rulings but provides the spiritual and motivational foundation for the study of Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
العلم (al-‘ilm): Islamic knowledge, particularly sacred knowledge (shar‘i ‘ilm) including Quran, hadith, fiqh, and related disciplines.
العالم (al-‘ālim): A scholar endowed with Islamic knowledge, especially one who acts upon it and teaches it.
التفقه في الدين (al-tafaqquh fī al-dīn): Gaining deep understanding of the religion, particularly in fiqh rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith quoted in this passage, who will intercede on the Day of Judgment?
A) Prophets, then scholars, then martyrs
B) Prophets, then martyrs, then scholars
C) Scholars, then prophets, then martyrs
D) Martyrs, then scholars, then prophets

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi tradition holds that the pursuit of sacred knowledge, especially fiqh, is an act of worship that elevates the scholar to a rank second only to prophets.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
The Superiority of the Scholar Over the Worshipper
Hadith compilation on scholar's virtue

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hadith comparing scholars to the full moon and explain the rank of scholars in intercession.

Core Idea
The scholar outshines the worshipper like a full moon over all stars.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah opens the study of fiqh with powerful hadith that elevate the status of knowledge and scholars. It is not a legal ruling but a motivational foundation. Understanding these virtues inspires the pursuit of Islamic knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the comparison
Find the hadith that compares the scholar to the full moon. Note that the worshipper is compared to other stars.
The full moon is the brightest and most distinct at night.
2
Understand intercession ranks
The hadith lists three groups that intercede: prophets, scholars, then martyrs. This places scholars just below prophets.
Martyrdom is highly praised, yet scholars rank above it.
3
List the five types of worshipful looking
The hadith mentions looking at parents, Quran, Kaaba, Zamzam, and the scholar. Each is an act of worship.
Looking at a scholar is a form of worship, emphasizing respect.
4
Examine the rewards for honoring scholars
The hadith state that honoring a scholar equals honoring seventy prophets, and honoring a student equals honoring seventy martyrs.
Loving scholars and knowledge erases sin according to the hadith.

Source Text

وقال : فَضْلُ العَالِم عَلَى العَابِدِ، كَفَضْلِ القَمَرِ ليلةَ البدرِ عَلَى سَائِرِ الكواكب ). وقال : يشفع يوم القيامةِ ثلاثة: الأنبياء، ثم العلماء، ثم الشهداء ) (). فأعظم بمرتبة هي تلو النبوة، وفـوق الشهادة، مع ما ورد في فضل الشهادة، وقال : ( مَنْ أَحَبَّ أنْ ينظر إلى عتقاءِ اللهِ مِنَ النَّارِ، فَلينظر إلى العُلَمَاءِ والمُتَعَلِّمِينَ ) (۳). وقال : ( خمس مِنَ النَّظَر عِبَادَةُ: النظر إلى الأبوين عبادة، والنظر في المصحفِ عبادة، والنظر إلى الكعبة عِبَادَةٌ، والنظرُ في زَمْزَمَ عِبادةٌ ، يحط الخطايـا حـطـا، والنظر إلى العالم عبادة » . وقال : ( مَنْ أكرمَ عَالِماً فَقَدْ أكرم سبعينَ نَبياً، ومَنْ أكرمَ متعلماً فقد أكرَمَ سبعينَ شهيداً، ومَنْ أَحَبَّ العِلْمَ والعُلَمَاءَ لا تُكْتَبُ عليهِ خَطِيئَةٌ أيامَ حَيَاتِهِ » . وقال : ( يَبْعَثُ اللَّهُ العباد يوم القيامةِ، ثُمَّ يميزُ العُلماء، فيقولُ: يا معشر العلماء، إني لم أضَعْ فِيكُمْ عِلْمِي إِلا لِعِلْمِي بِكُمْ، فَلَمْ أَضَعْ عِلْمِي فِيكُمْ لأعذبكُم، انطلقوا فقدْ غَفَرْتُ لَكُمْ . ثم قال عليه الصلاة والسلام: يقول الله تعالى لا تحقِرُوا عبدَاً لي آتِيتُهُ عِلْماً، فإني لم أحقره حين علمته . وعن مجاهد عن (۱) (V) عائشة ، أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «سألت جبريل عليه الصلاة والسلام عن ثواب العلماء، فقال: يـا محمد، إنَّ لله تعالى مدينةً تحت العرش من مسك أذفر لها جنات وأنهار، في جوفها سبعون ألف بيت من جوهر واحد، طول كل بيت ألف فرسخ، وعرضه مثل ذلك، في كل بيت ألف زاوية، في كـلّ زاوية ألف سرير، ومن السرير إلى السرير ألف ذراع، وعلى كل سرير ألف فراش، فــوق كــل فـراش ألف حوراء مِنَ الحور العين، وعلى كل واحدة ألف حلة، لا تواري حـلـة حـلـة، ولا يــاري الـحـلـل الجلد، ولا يواري الجلد اللحم، ولا يواري اللحم العظم، ولا يواري العظم المخ، يرى بعضـه مـن بعض، كما ترى السلكة في الياقوتة البيضاء، وعلى كل واحدة منهنَّ ثلاثة آلاف ذؤابة من المسكِ (۱) (۲) (۳) (٤) (٥) (٦) (۷) (1) أخرجه الترمذي في العلم، باب ما جاء في فضل الفقه على العبادة (۲۶۸۲) وأبو داود في العلـم، بـاب الحـث على طلب العلم (٣٦٤١). (۲) أخرجه ابن ماجه في الفتن، باب ذكر الشفاعة (٤۳۱۳)، والبيهقي في شعب الإيمان (۱۷۰۷). (۳) ذكره العجلوني في كشف الخفاء (۲۲۲/۲)، وقال: قال ابن حجر نقلاً عن السيوطي: كذب موضوع. (٤) الحديث مركب من عدة أحاديث بعضه أخرجه السيوطي في الجامع الصغير (٣٩٦٦)، وبعضه الديلمي في مسند الفردوس (٢٩٧/٤) وبعضه المناوي في الفيض القدير (٢٩٩/٦). (٥) ذكره ابن الجوزي في العلل المتناهية (۱۰۷/۱)، والديلمي في مسند الفردوس (٥٧٦/٣) مختصراً. (٦) أخرجه الطبراني في الأوسط (٣٠٢/٤). (۷) أخرجه البيهقي في المدخل إلى السنن الكبرى (٣٤٤/١) ، وابن عدي في الكامل (١١١/٤). -YA-  (1) والعنبر، يعطي الله تعالى، يا محمد، هذا الثواب للعلماء، وأفضلُ منْ هذا، وعلى باب المدينة ملك قائم، ينادي كلَّ يومٍ: أَلا مَنْ زَارَ عَالِمَاً فَقَدْ زَارَ نَبياً، ألا مَنْ زَارَ نَبياً فَلَهُ الجَنَّةُ، أَلا مَنْ نَظَرَ إلى وَجْهِ العَالِمِ، فَقَدْ نَظَرَ إِلى وَجْهِ مُحَمَّدٍ عليه الصلاة والسلام، ألا مَنْ نَظَرَ إلى محمدٍ، فَقَدْ نَظَرَ إِلَى اللَّهِ، وَمَنْ نَظَرَ إِلى اللهِ تَعَالَى فَلَهُ الجَنَّةُ، وَحَرَّمَ جَسَدَهُ عَلَى النَّارِ » ). وقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: « جُلُوسُ سَاعَةٍ عِنْدَ مذاكرةِ العِلْمِ خَيْرٌ مِنْ مَائَةِ أَلْفِ رَكْعَةٍ تَطَوعاً أو خِيرٌ مِنْ مَائَةِ أَلْفِ تَسْبِيحَةٍ وَخيرٌ مِنْ عَشَرَةِ آلافٍ فَرَسٍ يَغْزُو بِهَا الْمُؤْمِنُ . وقال : ( مَنْ خَرَجَ فِي طَلَبِ العِلْمِ فَهُوَ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ حَتَّى يَرْجِعَ» . مــن التاتارخانية». انتهى. وقال : « مَنْ غَدَا إلى المسجدِ لا يريد إلا أن يتعلَمَ خَيْراً أو يُعَلِّمَهُ، كَانَ لَهُ (٤) كأجر حاج تام حجته ). حدیث حسن أخرجه الطبراني، قاله الشيخ « أبو الحسـن البـكـري»، انتهى. ومنها، وقال : ( نصر الله عبداً سمع مقالتي، فحفظها، ووعاهَا، كما سمعها وأداهَا، فـــرب حامل فقه إلى غير فقيه، وربَّ حامل فقه إلى مَنْ هُوَ أفْقَهُ مِنْهُ ). وقال المعاذ لما بعثه إلى اليمن: « لأَنْ يَهْدِيَ اللَّهُ بِكَ رجُلاً وَاحِدَاً، خَيْرٌ لَكَ مِنَ الدُّنيا وَمَا فِيهَا ، وقال : ( مَنْ تَعَلَّمَ بَابَا مِنَ العِلْمِ ليعلم النَّاسَ، أُعطي ثواب سبعين نبياً صديقاً ). وقال : ( إنَّ الله وملائكته وأهل السموات والأرض حتى النملة في جحرها، وحتّى الحوت في البحر ليصلون على معلم الناس الخير ) .
And he said: The superiority of the scholar over the worshipper is like the superiority of the full moon over the rest of the stars. And he said: Three will intercede on the Day of Resurrection: the prophets, then the scholars, then the martyrs. So how great is a rank that is next to prophethood and above martyrdom, along with what has been reported regarding the virtue of martyrdom. And he said: Whoever loves to look at the freed slaves of Allah from the Fire, let him look at the scholars and the students. And he said: Five types of looking are worship: looking at one's parents is worship, looking in the Quran is worship, looking at the Kaaba is worship, looking at Zamzam is worship, it erases sins completely, and looking at the scholar is worship. And he said: Whoever honors a scholar has honored seventy prophets, and whoever honors a student has honored seventy martyrs, and whoever loves knowledge and scholars will not have a sin recorded for him during his life. And he said: Allah will resurrect the servants on the Day of Resurrection, then He will separate the scholars and say: O assembly of scholars, I did not place My knowledge in you except because of My knowledge of you, so I did not place My knowledge in you to punish you; go, for I have forgiven you. Then he, peace and blessings be upon him, said: Allah Almighty says: Do not belittle a servant of Mine to whom I have given knowledge, for I did not belittle him when I taught him. And from Mujahid, from Aisha, that the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: I asked Jibril, peace be upon him, about the reward of the scholars. He said: O Muhammad, indeed Allah Almighty has a city beneath the Throne made of pure musk; it has gardens and rivers; in its interior are seventy thousand houses of single jewel, the length of each house is a thousand farsakhs and its width is similar; in each house are a thousand corners; in each corner are a thousand couches; from couch to couch is a thousand cubits; on each couch are a thousand mattresses; on each mattress are a thousand houris from the wide-eyed maidens; on each one are a thousand garments; one garment does not cover another garment, nor do the garments cover the skin, nor does the skin cover the flesh, nor does the flesh cover the bone, nor does the bone cover the marrow; they see each other as you see a thread in a white ruby. On each one of them are three thousand locks of musk and ambergris. Allah Almighty gives, O Muhammad, this reward to the scholars, and better than this. At the gate of the city is a standing angel who calls out every day: Verily, whoever visits a scholar has visited a prophet; verily, whoever visits a prophet will have Paradise; verily, whoever looks at the face of a scholar has looked at the face of Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him; verily, whoever looks at Muhammad has looked at Allah; and whoever looks at Allah Almighty will have Paradise, and his body will be forbidden to the Fire. And the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: Sitting for an hour in a session of studying knowledge is better than a hundred thousand voluntary prayers, or better than a hundred thousand glorifications, and better than ten thousand horses with which a believer fights. And he said: Whoever goes out in search of knowledge is in the path of Allah until he returns. From al-Tatarkhaniyya. End. And he said: Whoever goes early to the mosque not wanting except to learn something good or teach it, will have the reward of a complete Hajj. A hasan hadith narrated by al-Tabarani, said by Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Bakri. End. And among them, he said: May Allah aid a servant who hears my words, then preserves them, understands them as he heard them, and conveys them; perhaps one who carries fiqh to one who is not a faqih, and perhaps one who carries fiqh to one who is more understanding than him. And he said to Mu'adh when he sent him to Yemen: If Allah guides one man through you, that is better for you than the world and everything in it. And he said: Whoever learns one chapter of knowledge to teach the people will be given the reward of seventy truthful prophets. And he said: Indeed, Allah and His angels and the inhabitants of the heavens and the earth, even the ant in its hole and even the fish in the sea, pray for the teacher of goodness.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of hadith and reports from the author of Imdad al-Fattah, used as introductory material to motivate the study of fiqh. It serves as a front matter, establishing the immense virtue of knowledge and scholars. The author quotes numerous prophetic traditions to elevate the status of scholars above mere worshippers, comparing them to the full moon among stars. He mentions that on the Day of Resurrection, prophets, scholars, and martyrs will intercede, placing scholars just below prophets and above martyrs. He then lists five types of looking that are considered worship, including looking at a scholar. The rewards for honoring scholars and students are immense—equated to honoring seventy prophets and seventy martyrs respectively. A lengthy hadith describes a magnificent city beneath the Throne prepared for scholars, with details of its construction and the reward for visiting or looking at a scholar. The author also cites hadith emphasizing the superiority of studying knowledge over supererogatory prayers and acts of worship. Going out in search of knowledge is akin to being in the path of Allah. Teaching and learning in the mosque earns the reward of a complete Hajj. The duty of conveying knowledge is stressed through the hadith of the Prophet about preserving and transmitting his words. The reward for guiding even one person is better than the entire world. Learning one chapter to teach earns the reward of seventy truthful prophets. Finally, the passage concludes that all creation prays for the teacher of goodness. These hadith collectively establish the foundational importance of seeking, teaching, and honoring knowledge in Islam, particularly in the Hanafi tradition where fiqh is highly esteemed.

Key Terms
عَالِم (‘ālim): A scholar of religious knowledge, particularly one who is knowledgeable in Islamic law and theology.
عِبَادَة (‘ibādah): Worship or acts of obedience to Allah; here, certain acts of looking are considered worship.
شَهَادَة (shahādah): Martyrdom; the status of one who dies in the path of Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in this passage, what is the comparison made between a scholar and a worshipper?
A) Like the sun and the moon
B) Like the full moon compared to all other stars
C) Like a king and a beggar
D) Like a river and a drop

Key Takeaway
The scholar holds a rank between prophecy and martyrdom, and honoring him is an act of worship that brings immense reward.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Rewards for Seeking and Teaching Knowledge
Hadith on reward for learning and teaching

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hadith about the city prepared for scholars and list the rewards for teaching and seeking knowledge mentioned in the passage.

Core Idea
Teaching knowledge earns the prayers of all creation and the reward of seventy prophets.

The second part of this front matter describes the magnificent reward prepared for scholars in the afterlife and the immense virtue of teaching and seeking knowledge. These hadith motivate the student to engage in learning and teaching with sincerity.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the description of the scholars' city
The hadith from Jibril describes a magnificent city under the Throne made of musk, with houses and couches. This is the reward for scholars.
The details emphasize the grandeur and beauty of the reward.
2
Understand the angel's call
An angel at the gate announces that visiting a scholar is like visiting a prophet, and looking at a scholar is like looking at Muhammad (saw).
This chain links respect for scholars to direct spiritual benefit.
3
Compare the rewards of studying and worship
Sitting for knowledge is better than 100,000 voluntary prayers or glorifications, and going out to seek knowledge is like being in the path of Allah.
This highlights the superiority of seeking knowledge over supererogatory acts.
4
Identify the rewards for teaching and conveying
Teaching in the mosque earns the reward of a complete Hajj. Learning one chapter to teach earns the reward of seventy truthful prophets. All creation prays for the teacher of goodness.
Teaching has a multiplier effect on reward.

وقال : فَضْلُ العَالِم عَلَى العَابِدِ، كَفَضْلِ القَمَرِ ليلةَ البدرِ عَلَى سَائِرِ الكواكب ). وقال : يشفع يوم القيامةِ ثلاثة: الأنبياء، ثم العلماء، ثم الشهداء ) (). فأعظم بمرتبة هي تلو النبوة، وفـوق الشهادة، مع ما ورد في فضل الشهادة، وقال : ( مَنْ أَحَبَّ أنْ ينظر إلى عتقاءِ اللهِ مِنَ النَّارِ، فَلينظر إلى العُلَمَاءِ والمُتَعَلِّمِينَ ) (۳). وقال : ( خمس مِنَ النَّظَر عِبَادَةُ: النظر إلى الأبوين عبادة، والنظر في المصحفِ عبادة، والنظر إلى الكعبة عِبَادَةٌ، والنظرُ في زَمْزَمَ عِبادةٌ ، يحط الخطايـا حـطـا، والنظر إلى العالم عبادة » . وقال : ( مَنْ أكرمَ عَالِماً فَقَدْ أكرم سبعينَ نَبياً، ومَنْ أكرمَ متعلماً فقد أكرَمَ سبعينَ شهيداً، ومَنْ أَحَبَّ العِلْمَ والعُلَمَاءَ لا تُكْتَبُ عليهِ خَطِيئَةٌ أيامَ حَيَاتِهِ » . وقال : ( يَبْعَثُ اللَّهُ العباد يوم القيامةِ، ثُمَّ يميزُ العُلماء، فيقولُ: يا معشر العلماء، إني لم أضَعْ فِيكُمْ عِلْمِي إِلا لِعِلْمِي بِكُمْ، فَلَمْ أَضَعْ عِلْمِي فِيكُمْ لأعذبكُم، انطلقوا فقدْ غَفَرْتُ لَكُمْ . ثم قال عليه الصلاة والسلام: يقول الله تعالى لا تحقِرُوا عبدَاً لي آتِيتُهُ عِلْماً، فإني لم أحقره حين علمته . وعن مجاهد عن (۱) (V) عائشة ، أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «سألت جبريل عليه الصلاة والسلام عن ثواب العلماء، فقال: يـا محمد، إنَّ لله تعالى مدينةً تحت العرش من مسك أذفر لها جنات وأنهار، في جوفها سبعون ألف بيت من جوهر واحد، طول كل بيت ألف فرسخ، وعرضه مثل ذلك، في كل بيت ألف زاوية، في كـلّ زاوية ألف سرير، ومن السرير إلى السرير ألف ذراع، وعلى كل سرير ألف فراش، فــوق كــل فـراش ألف حوراء مِنَ الحور العين، وعلى كل واحدة ألف حلة، لا تواري حـلـة حـلـة، ولا يــاري الـحـلـل الجلد، ولا يواري الجلد اللحم، ولا يواري اللحم العظم، ولا يواري العظم المخ، يرى بعضـه مـن بعض، كما ترى السلكة في الياقوتة البيضاء، وعلى كل واحدة منهنَّ ثلاثة آلاف ذؤابة من المسكِ (۱) (۲) (۳) (٤) (٥) (٦) (۷) (1) أخرجه الترمذي في العلم، باب ما جاء في فضل الفقه على العبادة (۲۶۸۲) وأبو داود في العلـم، بـاب الحـث على طلب العلم (٣٦٤١). And he said: The superiority of the scholar over the worshipper is like the superiority of the full moon over the rest of the stars. And he said: Three will intercede on the Day of Resurrection: the prophets, then the scholars, then the martyrs. So how great is a rank that is next to prophethood and above martyrdom, along with what has been reported regarding the virtue of martyrdom. And he said: Whoever loves to look at the freed slaves of Allah from the Fire, let him look at the scholars and the students. And he said: Five types of looking are worship: looking at one's parents is worship, looking in the Quran is worship, looking at the Kaaba is worship, looking at Zamzam is worship, it erases sins completely, and looking at the scholar is worship. And he said: Whoever honors a scholar has honored seventy prophets, and whoever honors a student has honored seventy martyrs, and whoever loves knowledge and scholars will not have a sin recorded for him during his life. And he said: Allah will resurrect the servants on the Day of Resurrection, then He will separate the scholars and say: O assembly of scholars, I did not place My knowledge in you except because of My knowledge of you, so I did not place My knowledge in you to punish you; go, for I have forgiven you. Then he, peace and blessings be upon him, said: Allah Almighty says: Do not belittle a servant of Mine to whom I have given knowledge, for I did not belittle him when I taught him. And from Mujahid, from Aisha, that the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: I asked Jibril, peace be upon him, about the reward of the scholars. He said: O Muhammad, indeed Allah Almighty has a city beneath the Throne made of pure musk; it has gardens and rivers; in its interior are seventy thousand houses of single jewel, the length of each house is a thousand farsakhs and its width is similar; in each house are a thousand corners; in each corner are a thousand couches; from couch to couch is a thousand cubits; on each couch are a thousand mattresses; on each mattress are a thousand houris from the wide-eyed maidens; on each one are a thousand garments; one garment does not cover another garment, nor do the garments cover the skin, nor does the skin cover the flesh, nor does the flesh cover the bone, nor does the bone cover the marrow; they see each other as you see a thread in a white ruby. On each one of them are three thousand locks of musk and ambergris. Allah Almighty gives, O Muhammad, this reward to the scholars, and better than this. At the gate of the city is a standing angel who calls out every day: Verily, whoever visits a scholar has visited a prophet; verily, whoever visits a prophet will have Paradise; verily, whoever looks at the face of a scholar has looked at the face of Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him; verily, whoever looks at Muhammad has looked at Allah; and whoever looks at Allah Almighty will have Paradise, and his body will be forbidden to the Fire. And the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: Sitting for an hour in a session of studying knowledge is better than a hundred thousand voluntary prayers, or better than a hundred thousand glorifications, and better than ten thousand horses with which a believer fights. And he said: Whoever goes out in search of knowledge is in the path of Allah until he returns. From al-Tatarkhaniyya. End. A hasan hadith narrated by al-Tabarani, said by Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Bakri. End. And he said: Whoever learns one chapter of knowledge to teach the people will be given the reward of seventy truthful prophets. Commentary
This passage is a compilation of hadith and reports from the author of Imdad al-Fattah, used as introductory material to motivate the study of fiqh. Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Virtue of Seeking Knowledge: Opening Hadiths
Prophetic hadiths on virtue of knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list at least three rewards mentioned in the hadiths for seeking or teaching knowledge, and explain why such hadiths are included in a fiqh commentary.

Core Idea
Seeking knowledge is among the greatest deeds, rewarded with Paradise and blessings from all creation.

This lesson presents a collection of hadiths that open the commentary of Nur al-Idah. These are not legal rulings but powerful motivators, reminding the student of the immense virtue and reward attached to learning and teaching sacred knowledge. Understanding their context helps us appreciate the high station of the scholar in Islam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the genre and purpose
Recognize that this passage is a compilation of hadiths (and a saying of Mu'adh) intended to encourage the reader by highlighting the merits of knowledge and teaching. It is not a source of legal rulings but a motivational preface.
2
Extract key rewards
Note each reward: visiting a scholar equals visiting a prophet; sitting in a study circle is better than 100,000 voluntary rak'ahs; going out to seek knowledge is like being in Allah's path; teaching earns the reward of a complete Hajj; conveying knowledge brings divine help; guiding one person is better than the whole world; learning to teach gives reward of seventy prophets; teacher receives blessings from all creation.
3
Recognize the chain of transmission references
The author cites sources like al-Tatar Khaniyya and al-Tabarani, and mentions Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Bakri's grading. This shows the scholarly care in citing these traditions.
4
Connect to fiqh study
Understand that these hadiths are placed here to inspire the student of fiqh. They remind us that the effort to learn fiqh is an act of worship with immense reward, and that teaching fiqh is a form of guidance.

والعنبر، يعطي الله تعالى، يا محمد، هذا الثواب للعلماء، وأفضلُ منْ هذا، وعلى باب المدينة ملك قائم، ينادي كلَّ يومٍ: أَلا مَنْ زَارَ عَالِمَاً فَقَدْ زَارَ نَبياً، ألا مَنْ زَارَ نَبياً فَلَهُ الجَنَّةُ، أَلا مَنْ نَظَرَ إلى وَجْهِ العَالِمِ، فَقَدْ نَظَرَ إِلى وَجْهِ مُحَمَّدٍ عليه الصلاة والسلام، ألا مَنْ نَظَرَ إلى محمدٍ، فَقَدْ نَظَرَ إِلَى اللَّهِ، وَمَنْ نَظَرَ إِلى اللهِ تَعَالَى فَلَهُ الجَنَّةُ، وَحَرَّمَ جَسَدَهُ عَلَى النَّارِ » ). وقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: « جُلُوسُ سَاعَةٍ عِنْدَ مذاكرةِ العِلْمِ خَيْرٌ مِنْ مَائَةِ أَلْفِ رَكْعَةٍ تَطَوعاً أو خِيرٌ مِنْ مَائَةِ أَلْفِ تَسْبِيحَةٍ وَخيرٌ مِنْ عَشَرَةِ آلافٍ فَرَسٍ يَغْزُو بِهَا الْمُؤْمِنُ . وقال : ( مَنْ خَرَجَ فِي طَلَبِ العِلْمِ فَهُوَ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ حَتَّى يَرْجِعَ» . مــن التاتارخانية». انتهى. وقال : « مَنْ غَدَا إلى المسجدِ لا يريد إلا أن يتعلَمَ خَيْراً أو يُعَلِّمَهُ، كَانَ لَهُ
(٤)
كأجر حاج تام حجته ). حدیث حسن أخرجه الطبراني، قاله الشيخ « أبو الحسـن البـكـري»، انتهى. ومنها، وقال : ( نصر الله عبداً سمع مقالتي، فحفظها، ووعاهَا، كما سمعها وأداهَا، فـــرب حامل فقه إلى غير فقيه، وربَّ حامل فقه إلى مَنْ هُوَ أَفْقَهُ مِنْهُ ). وقال المعاذ لما بعثه إلى اليمن: « لأَنْ يَهْدِيَ اللَّهُ بِكَ رجُلاً وَاحِدَاً، خَيْرٌ لَكَ مِنَ الدُّنيا وَمَا فِيهَا ، وقال : ( مَنْ تَعَلَّمَ بَابَا مِنَ العِلْمِ ليعلم النَّاسَ، أُعطي ثواب سبعين نبياً صديقاً ). وقال : ( إنَّ الله وملائكته وأهل السموات والأرض حتى النملة في جحرها، وحتّى الحوت في البحر ليصلون على معلم الناس الخير ) .
(1) And amber, Allah Almighty gives, O Muhammad, this reward to the scholars, and better than this, and at the gate of Medina there is an angel standing, calling every day: Indeed, whoever visits a scholar has indeed visited a prophet; indeed, whoever visits a prophet will have Paradise; indeed, whoever looks at the face of a scholar has indeed looked at the face of Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him; indeed, whoever looks at Muhammad has indeed looked at Allah; and whoever looks at Allah Almighty will have Paradise, and his body will be forbidden from the Fire. And the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Sitting for an hour in discussion of knowledge is better than one hundred thousand voluntary rak'ahs, or better than one hundred thousand glorifications, and better than ten thousand horses a believer goes to battle on.' And he said: 'Whoever goes out in search of knowledge is in the path of Allah until he returns.' From al-Tatar Khaniyya. End. And he said: 'Whoever goes to the mosque desiring only to learn good or teach it, will have the reward of a complete Hajj.' A good hadith narrated by al-Tabarani, said by Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Bakri, end. And from them, and he said: 'May Allah grant victory to a servant who hears my words, memorizes them, understands them as he heard them, and conveys them; for many a carrier of fiqh is not a faqih, and many a carrier of fiqh conveys to one more knowledgeable than him.' And he said concerning Mu'adh when he sent him to Yemen: 'If Allah guides a single man through you, it is better for you than the world and everything in it.' And he said: 'Whoever learns a chapter of knowledge in order to teach people will be given the reward of seventy truthful prophets.' And he said: 'Indeed, Allah, His angels, the inhabitants of the heavens and the earth, even the ant in its hole, and even the fish in the sea, send blessings upon the teacher of good to people.'
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of hadiths and sayings about the virtue of knowledge, drawn from various sources to encourage learning and teaching. The author begins with a lengthy hadith about the merits of scholars, then quotes several prophetic traditions: sitting in a study circle is better than immense acts of worship; going out to seek knowledge is like being in the path of Allah; going to the mosque to learn or teach earns the reward of a complete Hajj; conveying knowledge brings divine assistance; guiding others is better than all worldly goods; learning a chapter to teach earns the reward of seventy prophets; and Allah and all creation bless the teacher of good. These are not legal rulings but motivational material placed at the beginning of the commentary to inspire the reader.

Key Terms
مذاكرة العلم (mudhākarat al-ʿilm): Discussing and reviewing knowledge in a study circle

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Better than performing Hajj a hundred times

Key Takeaway
Seeking knowledge and teaching it are among the greatest acts of worship, rewarded with infinite blessings and divine favor.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Seven Methods of Beginning a Classical Hanafi Work
Author's supplication and methodological note on book prefaces

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the seven methods of beginning a book according to Shaykh al-Naqshbandi and distinguish the three obligatory from the four permissible.

Core Idea
A Hanafi book's introduction follows a structured etiquette: obligatory praise and blessings, then optional acknowledgments.

This passage, from the conclusion of Imdad al-Fattah's introduction, offers a rare methodological note: it lists seven ways to begin a classical composition. Understanding this etiquette helps you read and write prefaces with the same scholarly discipline that governs fiqh itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three obligatory methods
List the three elements the author says are 'obligatory to use' (واجبة الاستعمال): the basmala (بسم الله), the hamdala (الحمد لله), and the salawat (الصلاة على النبي). Note that 'obligatory' here means customary necessity for a proper preface, not a legal obligation.
2
Identify the four permissible methods
List the four elements the author says are 'permissible to use' (جائزة الاستعمال): mentioning the reason for writing, naming the book, praising the subject of the book, and describing the author's circumstance in summary.
3
Understand the rationale for categorisation
The three 'obligatory' ones are acts of worship and gratitude that establish the tone of the work. The four permissible ones are contextual and vary depending on the work's purpose.
The author says 'the reasoning has already been presented' — referring to earlier justification for starting with praise and blessings.
4
Apply the framework to a hypothetical work
Imagine a Hanafi fiqh manual. Write a mock preface containing all three obligatory elements and two of the permissible ones. This will help you internalise the structure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالله أَسْأَلُ أَنْ يَنْفَعَ بِهِ عِبَادَهُ، وَيُدِيمَ بِهِ الْإِفَادَةُ.
( والله) الكريم ( أسأل)، وبحبيبه المصطفى أتوسل، أن ينفع به عباده) على الدوام، (ويديـم بـه الإفادة) بمدد النبي عليه أفضل الصلاة والسلام.
تنبيه: قال الشيخ الإمام «شهاب الدين النقشبندي»، رحمه الله : للفضلاء في ابتداء التأليف سبع طرائق ثلاثة منها واجبة الاستعمال: البسملة، ثم الحمدلة، ثم الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم والوجـه قـد تقدم. وأربعة جائزة الاستعمال، ذكر باعث التأليف، وتسمية الكتاب، ومدح الفن الذي فيه التأليف، وذكر كيفية وقوع المؤلف إجمالاً. وهذا أوان الشروع في المقصود بعون الملك المعبود.
-.-
And Allah I ask to benefit His servants through it, and to perpetuate benefit through it. (And Allah) the Generous (I ask), and through His Chosen Beloved I seek intercession, that He benefit His servants through it perpetually, and perpetuate benefit through it by the support of the Prophet, upon him the best of prayers and peace. Cautionary note: The Imam, Shaykh Shihab al-Din al-Naqshbandi, may Allah have mercy on him, said: For the virtuous, in beginning a composition, there are seven methods, three of which are obligatory to use: the basmala, then the hamdala, then the prayer upon the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and the reasoning has already been presented. And four are permissible to use: mentioning the motivation for composition, naming the book, praising the art in which the composition is undertaken, and mentioning the author's circumstance in summary. And this is the time to begin the intended subject with the help of the Worshipped King.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage concludes the introduction of the commentary. The author first offers a supplication to Allah, asking that the book benefit readers and that the benefit be continuous, and he seeks intercession through the Prophet. Then he includes a cautionary note quoting Shaykh Shihab al-Din al-Naqshbandi, who outlines seven methods for beginning a book: three are obligatory (basmala, hamdala, and salawat upon the Prophet) and four are permissible (mentioning the reason for writing, naming the book, praising the subject, and briefly describing how the work came to be). The author then states that he is about to begin the main subject of the book.

Key Terms
البسملة (al-basmala): Saying 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' (In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful).
الحمدلة (al-ḥamdala): Saying 'Alhamdulillah' (All praise is due to Allah).
الصلاة على النبي (al-ṣalāt ʿalā al-nabī): Sending blessings upon the Prophet Muhammad, e.g. 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Shaykh al-Naqshbandi, how many methods of beginning a book are obligatory?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Seven

Key Takeaway
Classical Hanafi authors followed a standard preface structure with three required elements (basmala, hamdala, salawat) and four optional ones.

Understanding the Khatimah: The Colophon of 'Imdad al-Fattah'
Colophon of 'Imdad al-Fattah' with author's humility and dates.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key components of a classical Hanafi fiqh book's conclusion and explain the significance of the dates and prayers recorded in the colophon.

Core Idea
The colophon anchors the work in time, place, and piety—linking the author's effort to divine grace.

This lesson examines the conclusion (khatimah) of 'Imdad al-Fattah Sharh Nur al-Idah'. While it may appear as mere closing remarks, the colophon is a rich source of historical data and spiritual humility. Understanding it helps us appreciate the tradition of scholarly transmission and the author's relationship with his teachers and his Lord.

Guided Path
1
Locate the author's self-description
Find the phrases where the author humbles himself (e.g., 'al-ajiz al-haqir'). Understand the convention of self-deprecation in Islamic scholarship.
2
Identify the dates
The passage records three dates: completion of the matn, start and draft of the sharh, and the fair copy. Extract each and note the month and year.
3
Recognize the prayers
The author includes praises of Allah, blessings on the Prophet, and supplications for acceptance. These are standard but reflect the author's intention.
4
Note the chains of transmission
The author mentions the instruction from a 'gnostic' (arif). This shows that the work was not undertaken alone but with spiritual guidance.
5
Understand the structure
The conclusion also indicates what follows in the book (the book of Zakat), showing the arrangement of the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خاتمة الكتاب» وهذا ما تيسر للعاجز الحقير بعناية مولاه القوي القدير، الحمد لله الذي هدانا لهذا، وما كنا لنهتدي لولا أن هدانا الله، وصلى الله على سيدنا ومولانا محمد، خاتم أنبيائه، وعلى آله وصحبه وذريَّتِهِ ومَنْ والاهُ ونسألُ اللهَ، سبحانَهُ، مَتَوَسِّلِينَ أنْ يجعله خالصاً لوجهه الكريم، وأن ينفع به النَّفْعَ العَمِيمَ، وَيُجْزِلَ بِهِ الثّوابَ الجَسيم على باب) ملك أو وزير عظيم أو كبير عظيم لحاجة) يقدر على قضائهـا عــادة، (فالمعتكف يقولُ) لسان حاله إن لم ينطق بذلك لسان قاله: (لا أبرح) قائماً بباب مولاي سائلاً منه جميع مأربي وكشف مـا نزل بي من الكرب، وصار مصاحبي وتجنبي لذلك أعز إخواني، بل عين قرابتي (حتى يَغْفِرَ لي ذنوبي التي هي سبب بعدي ونزول مصائبي، ثم يفيض بمنته علي بما يليق بأهليته وكرمه، إكرام من التجأ إلى منيع حرزه وحرمه، وهذه إشارة إلى أن العبد الذليل الجامع لهذه المسائل، واقف بـبـاب مـولاه عـريـاً عــن الأعمال والفضائل، متوجهاً إليه سبحانه وتعالى بأعظم الوسائل، ماداً أكف الافتقار ، ملحـاً بالدعــاء والمسائل، مطرحاً على أعتاب باب الله تعالى، مرتجياً شفاعته غداً عنده بمـا وعــده بـه وهـو خـيـر کـافل، (وهذا ما تيسر ) جمعه من الشرح والمتن، (للعاجز الحقير ) ولم يكن إلا ( بعناية مولاه القوي القدير، الحمد لله الذي هدانا لهذا وما كنا لنهتدي لولا أن هدانا الله، وصلى الله على سيدنا ومولانا محمد خاتم أنبيائه، وعلى آله وصحبه وذريَّتِهِ ومن والاه. ونسألُ اللهَ، سبحانَهُ، مَتَوَسَلينَ) إلـيـه بـالنبي المصطفى الرحيم، (أنْ يجعله) وما من به من هذا الشرح (خالصاً لوجهه الكريم، وأن ينفــع بـه) وبشـرحـه هـذا ( النَّفْعَ العَمِيمَ، ويُجْزِلَ به) وبشرحه ( النواب الجسيم)، وأن يغفر لنا ولوالدينا ومشايخنا وإخواننـا وذريتنا، وأن يستر عيوبنا ويرزقنا ما تقر به عيوننا. حالاً ومالاً آمين. وكان ابتداء جمـع هـذا الشرح المبارك في منتصف شهر ربيع الأول سنة خمس وأربعين وألف بإشارة بعض العارفين وأمره بجمعه، جمعنا الله وإياه بدار السلام بسلام، وخُتِم جمعه في المسودة بختام شهر رجب الحرام بذلك العام، وكــان انتهاء تأليف متنه في يوم الجمعة المبارك رابع عشر من جمادى الأولى سنة اثنين وثلاثين وألف، وكنت أتمنى شرحه فلم تتيسر تلك المدة، حتى اجتمعت بهذا العارف الرباني وأشار، بل أمر، بذلك فيسر الله سبحانه وتعالى الشروع في إثر أمره، وأعان بلطفه وقدرته، فلله الحمد والشكر على جزيـل نـعـمـتـه وقـد وافق الفراغ من تبييض هذا الشرح المسمى بـ: « إمداد الفتاح شرح نور الإيضاح ونجاة الأرواح» في مثل أيام البداءة فيه في منتصف شهر ربيع الأول، وهو الثاني عشر يوم الخميس المبارك، بإشارة سيد البشر سنة ست وأربعين وألف، أحسن الله ختامها. وصلى الله على سيدنا ومولانا محمد وعلى سائر الأنبياء والمرسلين وعلى آلهم وصحبهم والتابعين، وتابعيهم بإحسان إلى يوم الدين، ويليه كتاب الزكاة إلى آخر الشرح، من الشرح الصغير للشيخ شارح هذا الشرح الكبير.
Conclusion of the book. This is what was facilitated for the wretched and insignificant one through the care of his Mighty and Powerful Lord. Praise be to Allah who guided us to this, and we would not have been guided unless Allah guided us. May Allah bless our master Muhammad, the Seal of the Prophets, and his family, Companions, and descendants, and those who support him. And we ask Allah, glorified be He, making intercession, to make it purely for His noble face, and to grant widespread benefit through it, and to bestow immense reward... (then a repetition of the earlier i'tikaf analogy)... And this is what was facilitated to collect from the explanation and the text, for the wretched and insignificant one. And it was only through the care of his Mighty and Powerful Lord... And the beginning of collecting this blessed explanation was in the middle of Rabi' al-Awwal 1045 AH by the indication of one of the gnostics and his command to compile it... And it was completed in draft at the end of Rajab al-Haram of that year. The composition of its text was completed on Friday, 14 Jumada al-Ula 1032 AH... And the final copying of this explanation named 'Imdad al-Fattah Sharh Nur al-Idah wa Najat al-Arwah' was finished on the same date as its beginning, in the middle of Rabi' al-Awwal, on Thursday, 12th, 1046 AH... May Allah bless our master Muhammad and all the prophets and messengers, and their families, companions, followers, and those who follow them in righteousness until the Day of Judgment. Next follows the Book of Zakat until the end of the explanation, from the small explanation of the author of this large explanation.
Source pages p. 681

Commentary
This is the conclusion (khatimah) of the book 'Imdad al-Fattah Sharh Nur al-Idah'. The author humbly describes himself as 'wretched and insignificant' and credits Allah's care for making the work possible. He praises Allah for guidance, sends blessings on the Prophet, and prays that the work be accepted. A unusual repetition of the i'tikaf analogy appears, likely a scribal duplication. He then lists the dates: the matn (text) was completed on Friday, 14 Jumada al-Ula 1032 AH; the compilation (jama') of the sharh started in mid-Rabi' al-Awwal 1045 AH at the behest of a gnostic, and the draft was finished at the end of Rajab 1045 AH. The final fair copy was completed on Thursday, 12th (mid-Rabi' al-Awwal) 1046 AH. He also notes that the book of Zakat will follow in the small sharh by the same author. This is standard colophon material showing the timeline and the author's devotion.

Key Terms
الخاتمة (al-khatimah): The concluding section of the book, containing the author's final remarks, prayers, and colophon.
الشرح (al-sharh): The commentary/explanation (this work) on the matn 'Nur al-Idah'.
العاجز الحقير (al-ajiz al-haqir): The wretched and insignificant one – a conventional expression of humility used by the author in the colophon.
العارف (al-arif): A gnostic, a spiritually accomplished person who guided the author to compile the commentary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The colophon of 'Imdad al-Fattah' records the author's reliance on Allah, the timeline of the work, and the spiritual motivation behind its compilation.

Introduction and Front Matter

The Colophon of Imdad al-Fattah: Dating and Scribe
Colophon marking completion of the manuscript

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to extract and interpret the key details from a Hanafi fiqh manuscript colophon, including date, scribe, and prayers.

Core Idea
A manuscript's colophon provides crucial evidence for its authorship and date of completion.

This lesson examines the colophon of Imdad al-Fattah, a Hanafi fiqh text. Colophons are the scribe's signature, often containing a date, name, and prayers. Understanding them helps authenticate and situate classical works within the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the completion date
Note the exact day, month, and year mentioned. The colophon states 'the last night of Ramadan, 1108 AH'.
Ramadan last night = 29 or 30 Ramadan. 1108 AH corresponds to 1697 CE.
2
Identify the scribe
Note the full name and humble self-description: 'Ali bin Muhammad al-Mulla al-Hamawi', calling himself 'the weakest of creation'.
The humility reflects Islamic scholarly tradition.
3
Identify the prayer
Note the request for mercy for himself and anyone who prays for him.
Common scribal invocation indicating piety.
4
Consider historical significance
Reflect on how this colophon helps date and authenticate the text, and what it reveals about the manuscript's chain.
Dating is vital for understanding which recension or commentary is being used.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكان الفراغ من كتابة هذا الكتاب ليلة الاثنين المبارك آخر ليلة من شهر رمضان المعظم قدرة من شهور سنة ١١٠٨هـ ألف ومائة وثمانية على يد أضعف الورى المحتاج إلى عفو الملك الغفار علي بن محمد الملا الحموي رحمه الله ومن دعا له بالرحمة آمين. تم بحمد الله تعالى
And the completion of writing this book was on the blessed Monday night, the last night of the month of Ramadan, the great in value, of the months of the year 1108 AH, by the hand of the weakest of creation, in need of the pardon of the Magnificent Forgiver, Ali bin Muhammad al-Mulla al-Hamawi, may Allah have mercy on him and on whoever prays for mercy upon him. Amen. It is completed by the praise of Allah Almighty.
Source pages p. 709

Commentary
This is the colophon of the book, providing the date and scribe's name. It notes that the manuscript was completed on the last night of Ramadan, 1108 AH (corresponding to 1697 CE), by Ali bin Muhammad al-Mulla al-Hamawi, who humbly describes himself as the weakest of creation. This information is valuable for understanding the provenance and dating of the text.

Key Terms
الفراغ (al-farāgh): Completion of writing the manuscript.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 1108 AH
B) 1200 AH
C) 1000 AH
D) 1300 AH

Key Takeaway
The colophon of Imdad al-Fattah records its completion by Ali al-Hamawi in 1108 AH, affirming the text's temporal context.

Navigating the Biographical Index of Imdad al-Fattah
List of scholar biographies with name, dates, works, and source references.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to locate a scholar's biographical entry in the index, identify their madhhab and major works, and explain the relevance of their authority to the commentary.

Core Idea
A scholar's biography establishes authority. Know their madhhab and works to trust their citations.

In classical fiqh commentaries like Imdad al-Fattah, authors often include a biographical index of scholars they cite. This index is not just a list; it is a tool to verify the reliability and context of each authority. Understanding how to read these entries helps you assess the strength of citations and avoid anachronism.

Guided Path
1
Locate the Scholar
Find the scholar by their kunyah or nisbah; the entries are alphabetically arranged. For example, 'Ibn Qudamah' appears under 'ابن قدامة'.
2
Extract the Full Name
Note the full name and any honorifics (e.g., 'Abdullah ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Qudamah al-Maqdisi al-Hanbali, Abu Muhammad Muwaffaq al-Din').
The full name helps distinguish scholars with similar names.
3
Identify the Madhhab
Each entry often indicates the school (e.g., 'al-Hanbali'). If not given, deduce from works or the list of teachers. For example, 'Ibn Qudamah' is explicitly labeled 'al-Hanbali'.
This is crucial for understanding the perspective of the citation.
4
Record Key Dates and Works
Note birth and death dates (AH) and major works. For 'Ibn Qudamah', dates are 541–620 AH and works include 'al-Mughni' and 'al-Burhan fi Ulum al-Quran'.
Dates help contextualize the scholar's era relative to the commentary.
5
Assess Relevance to the Commentary
Determine if the scholar is a Hanafi authority (if the commentary is Hanafi) or a figure cited for comparison. For instance, 'Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi' is a Hanafi faqih, so his works directly support the commentary's arguments.

ابن قدامة - عبد الله بن أحمد بن محمد بن قدامة المقدسي الحنبلي أبو محمد موفق الدين، من تصانيفه: المغني، البرهان في علوم القرآن، ولد سنة (٥٤١هـ ) وتوفي سنة (٦٢٠هـ) ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (٣٠/٦). ٣٤ ابن قيم الجوزية = محمد بن أبي بكر : هو الإمام محمد بن أبي بكر بن أيوب الزرعي الدمشقي شمس الدين المعروف بـ ( ابن قيم الجوزية) توفي سنة (٧٥١هـ ) اهـ. الأعلام (۸۷۱/۳). ٣٥- ابن كثير - عبد الله بن كثير بن عمرو بن عبد الله بن هرمز، مقرئ مكة المكرمة وأحد القراء السبعة، ولد سنة (٤٨هـ) وتوفي سنة (١٢٠هـ) ا.هـ السير (٣١٨/٥). ٣٦- ابن كج = يوسف بن أحمد بن كج الشافعي، القاضي أبو القاسم الدينوري، من تصانيفه: التجريد. توفي سنة (٤٠٥هـ ) الطبقات الشافعية (۱۹۸/۲). ۳۷- ابن كمال باشا = أحمد بن سليمان الرومي، من تصانيفه: الإصلاح والإيضاح ، توفي سنة (٩٤٠هـ ) ا.هـ الفوائد البهية (٤٤). ۳۸- ابن ماجه - محمد بن يزيد بن ماجه الربعي بالولاء أبو عبد الله، محدث، مفسر، من تصانيفه: كتاب السنن، تفسیر القرآن، ولد سنة (٢٠٩هـ) وتوفي سنة (٢٢٣هـ) ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (١١٥/١٢). ۳۹- ابن مالك - محمد بن عبد الله بن مالك الطائي الأندلسي الجياني أبو عبد الله النحوي اللغوي شارك في الفقه والأصول والحديث من تصانيفه: إكمال الأعلام بمثلث الكلام، تسهيل الفوائد وتكميل المقاصد ولد سنة (٦٠٠هـ) وتوفي سنة (٦٧٢هـ) ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (٢٣٤/١٠). ٤٠ - ابن ملك - عبد اللطيف بن عبد العزيز الشهير بابن ملك، فقيه، أصولي، صوفي، من تصانيفه: شرح كتاب المنار، مبارق الأزهار شرح مشارق الأنوار، توفي سنة (۸۰۱هـ) ا.هـ الفوائد البهية (۱۸۱). ٤١- ابن هشام - عبد الله بن يوسف بن أحمد بن عبد الله بن هشام الأنصاري جمال الدين أبو محمد النحوي شارك في المعاني والبيان والعروض من تصانيفه قطر الندى وبل الصدى مغني اللبيب ولد سنة (۷۰۸هـ) وتوفي سنة (٧٦١هـ) ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (١٣٦/٦). ٤٢- ابن وهبان = عبد الوهاب بن أحمد بن وهبان قاضي القضاة أبو محمد الدمشقي ولد قبل ثلاثين وسبعمائة وتوفي سنة (٧٦٨هـ)، من تصانيفه : المنظومة ضمنها غرائب المسائل في مذهب الحنفية، وشرحها في مجلدين وهـو نـظـم جـيـد متمكن اهـ. الفوائد البهية (۱۹۱). ٤٣- أبو الأسود - ظالم بن عمرو بن سفيان بن جندل الدولي، واضع علم النحو، فقيه، شاعر. من تصانيفه: ديوان شعر، ولد سنة (٦٦ق.هـ) وتوفي سنة (٦٩هـ) ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (٤٧/٥). ٤٤- أبو الحسن البكري - محمد بن عبد الرحمن البكري الصديقي، أبو الحسن، صوفي، مفسر، ناظم، من تصانيفه: تحفة واهب المواهب، الواضح الوجيز في تفسير القرآن العزيز، ولد سنة (٨٩٨هـ) وتوفي سنة (٩٥٢هـ ) ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (۱۳۷۱). ٤٥ - أبو العباس القرطبي = أحمد بن عمر بن إبراهيم بن عمر القرطبي، يعرف في بلاده بابن المزين، محدث، فقیه، من تصانيفه: مختصر الصحيحين، كشف القناع عن الوجد والسماع، ولد سنة (٥٧٨هـ) وتوفي سنة (٦٥٦هـ) ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (٢٧/٢). ٤٦- أبو الليث = نصر بن محمد السمرقندي: أبو الليث فقيه ،مفسر، محدث، حافظ، توفي سنة (٣٧٥هـ) من تصانيفه: النوازل، خزانة الفقه اهـ. السير (٣٢٢/١٦). ٤٧ - أبو المطيع = الحكم بن عبد الله: هو الإمام الحكم بن عبد الله بن مسلمة بن عبد الرحمـن القـاضـي أبـو مطيـع البلخي، راوي الفقه الأكبر عن أبي حنيفة، توفي سنة (۱۹۹هـ) اهـ. الفوائد البهية (۱۱۸). ٤٨- أبو اليسر البزدوي = محمد بن محمد البزدوي: أبو اليسر انتهت إليه مشيخة الحنفية، توفي سنة (٤٩٣هـ) من تصانيفه: المبسوط اهـ. هدية العارفين (۷۷/۲). ٤٩- أبو بكر الفضلي - ٥٢- أبو بكر بن علي الحدادي: العبادي المعروف بالحدادي شرح كتاب القدوري وسماه السراج الوهاج ثم اختصره، وسماه الجوهرة النيرة، توفي حدود سنة (٨٠٠هـ) اهـ كشف الظنون (١٦٣١/٢). ٥٣- أبو جعفر = محمد بن عبد الله بن محمد بن عمر أبو جعفر الهندواني إمام كبير كان يقال له: أبو حنيفة الصغير، توفي سنة (٣٦٢هـ ) اهـ. الجواهر المضية (١٩٣/٣). ٥٤ - أبو حاتم . - محمد بن حبان بن أحمد بن حبان التميمي البستي أبو حاتم، محدث، مؤرخ، من تصانيفه: الصحيح في الحديث، الطبقات الأصبهانية، ولد سنة ( ٢٧٠هـ) وتوفي سنة (٣٥٤هـ ) .ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (۱۷۳/۹). ٥٥- أبو حفص السفكردري، كان شيخاً كبيراً زاهداً متورعاً معتمداً سمع منه الشيخ الزندويستي ا.هـ الفوائد البهية (۱۱۷). ٥٦- أبو حفص الكبير = أحمد بن حفص: المعروف بأبي حفص الكبير وتوصيفه بالكبير بالنسبة إلى ابنه فإنه يكنى بأبي حفص الصغير (محمد بن أحمد بن حفص) شيخ ما وراء النهر ولد سنة (١٥٠هـ) وتوفي سنة (٢١٧هـ) اهـ السير (١٥٧/١٠). ٥٧ - أبو حفص النسفي - عمر بن محمد بن أحمد بن إسماعيل النسفي أبو حفص نجم الدين، فقیه، محدث، مفسر، من تصانيفه: مجمع العلوم، ونظم الجامع الصغير للشيباني في الفقه الحنفي، ولد سنة (٤٦١هـ) وتوفي سنة (٥٣٧هـ) ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (٣٠٥/٧). أخذ عن إسماعيل بن حماد بن أبي حنيفة، أبو داود - سليمان بن الأشعث بن إسحاق بن بشير بن شداد الأزدي السجستاني أبو داود، محدث، فقيه، مـن تصانيفه: كتاب السنن المراسيل. ولد سنة (٢٠٢هـ) وتوفي سنة (٢٧٥هـ) ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (٢٥٥/٤). ٥٩ - أبو زيد = عبيد الله بن عمر بن عيسى: القاضي أبو زيد الدبوسي نسبة إلى دبوسية وهو أول من وضع علم الخلاف من تصانيفه: الأسرار، تقويم الأدلة، توفي ببخارى سنة (٤٣٠هـ ) لهـ الفوائد البهية (١٨٤). ٦٠- أبو سعيد البردعي - أحمد بن الحسين: القاضي أبو سعيد البردعي أ قتل سنة (۳۱۷هـ) في وقعة القرامطة مع الحجاج .اهـ. الفوائد البهية (ص٤٠). ٦١ - أبو شجاع - محمد بن أحمد بن حمزة بن الحسين بن علي بن علي بن أبي طالب المشهور بالسيد أبي شجاع كان عصر ركن الإسلام علي بن الحسين السغدي بسمرقند وكان الإمام الحسن الماتريدي معاصراً لهما وكان المعتبر في زمانهم في الفتاوى أن يجتمع خطهم عليها ا.هـ الفوائد البهية (٢٥٥) والجواهر المضية (٢٨/٣). ٦٢- أبو طالب المكي . - محمد بن علي بن عطية الحارثي المكي أبو طالب ،صوفي متكلم، من تصانيفه: قوت القلوب في معاملة المحبوب، وصف طريق المريد إلى مقام التوحيد، توفي سنة (٣٨٦هـ ) ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (۲۷/۱۱). ٦٣ - أبو عبيدة - معمر بن المثنى التيمي أبو عبيدة، أديب لغوي، نحوي، من تصانيفه معاني القرآن، نقائض جرير والفرزدق، ولد سنة (١١٠هـ) وتوفي سنة (٢٠٩هـ) ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (۳۰۹/۱۲). ٦٤ - أبو علي الجوزجاني = موسى بن سليمان الجوزجاني، أخذ الفقه عن محمد، وكتب مسائل الأصول والأمالي، توفي بعد المائتين ا.هـ الفوائد البهية (٣٥٤). ٦٥- أبو علي الدقاق قرأ على موسى بن نصر الرازي وهو أستاذ أبي سعيد البردعي وله كتاب الحيض. ا.هـ الفوائد البهية (۲۳۷). ٦٦ - أبو عمرو - زبان بن العلاء بن عمار بن عبد الله بن العريان التميمي، شيخ القرا ـة برز في الحروف وفي النحو وتصدر للإفادة مدة، ولد سنة ( ٧٠هـ) وتوفي سنة (١٥٤هـ)، ا.هـ السير (٤٠٧/٦). ٦٧- أبو نصر البغدادي - الأقطع - أحمد بن محمد. ٦٨ - أبي بكر بن عبد الرحمن بن الحارث بن هشام بن المغير ولد في خلافة عمر بن الخطاب له، وتوفي سنة (٩٤هـ) وكان يسمى راهب قريش .ا.هـ طبقات الفقهاء (٤١/١). ٦٩ - أبي يعلى - أحمد بن علي بن المثنى بن يحيى بن عيسى الموصلي أبو يعلى، محدث، من تصانيفه: المسند، المعجم، ولد سنة (٢١٠هـ) وتوفي سنة (٣٠٧هـ ) ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (۱۷/۲). ۷۰ - الأجمهوري - علي بن زين العابدين بن محمد بن عبد الرحمن الأجمهوري نور الدين أبو الأرشاد. من تصانيفه: شرح ألفية ابن مالك، شرح التهذيب للتفتازاني في المنطق ولد سنة (٩٦٧هـ) وتوفي سنة (١٠٦٦هـ ) ا.هـ هدية العارفين (٧٥٨/٢).

Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (4/255). 59 - Abu Zayd = Ubaydullah ibn Umar ibn Isa: al-Qadi Abu Zayd al-Dabusi, attributed to Dabusi, he is the first to write on the science of ikhtilaf, from his works: al-Asrar, Taqwim al-Adillah, died in Bukhara 430 AH. End. al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah (184). 60- Abu Sa'id al-Barda'i - Ahmad ibn al-Husayn: al-Qadi Abu Sa'id al-Barda'i was killed in 317 AH in the Qaramita incident with the pilgrims. End. al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah (40). 61 - Abu Shuja' - Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Hamzah ibn al-Husayn ibn Ali ibn Ali ibn Abi Talib, known as al-Sayyid Abu Shuja', he was a contemporary of Rukn al-Islam Ali ibn al-Husayn al-Sughdi in Samarqand and Imam al-Hasan al-Maturidi was their contemporary, and the accepted practice in their time for fatwas was that their signatures be gathered on them. End. al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah (255) and al-Jawahir al-Mudiyyah (3/28). 62- Abu Talib al-Makki - Muhammad ibn Ali ibn Atiyyah al-Harithi al-Makki Abu Talib, sufi, theologian, from his works: Qut al-Qulub fi Mu'amalat al-Mahbub, and Wasf Tariq al-Murid ila Maqam al-Tawhid, died 386 AH. End. Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (11/27). 63 - Abu Ubaydah - Muammar ibn al-Muthanna al-Taymi Abu Ubaydah, literary scholar, linguist, grammarian, from his works: Ma'ani al-Quran, Naqa'id Jarir wa al-Farazdaq, born 110 AH, died 209 AH. End. Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (12/309). 64 - Abu Ali al-Juzjani = Musa ibn Sulayman al-Juzjani, took fiqh from Muhammad, and wrote Masail al-Usul and al-Amali, died after 200. End. al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah (354). 65- Abu Ali al-Duqqaq studied under Musa ibn Nasr al-Razi, and he was the teacher of Abu Sa'id al-Barda'i, and he has the book al-Hayd. End. al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah (237). 66 - Abu Amr - Zaban ibn al-'Ala' ibn Ammar ibn Abdullah ibn al-'Uryan al-Tamimi, master of recitation, excelled in letters and grammar, and headed for teaching for a period, born 70 AH, died 154 AH. End. al-Siyar (6/407). 67- Abu Nasr al-Baghdadi - al-Aqta' - Ahmad ibn Muhammad. 68 - Abu Bakr ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Harith ibn Hisham ibn al-Mughirah, born in the caliphate of Umar ibn al-Khattab, died 94 AH, and was called the monk of Quraysh. End. Tabaqat al-Fuqaha' (1/41). 69 - Abu Ya'la - Ahmad ibn Ali ibn al-Muthanna ibn Yahya ibn Isa al-Mawsili Abu Ya'la, hadith scholar, from his works: al-Musnad, al-Mu'jam, born 210 AH, died 307 AH. End. Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (2/17). 70 - al-Ajhuri - Ali ibn Zayn al-Abidin ibn Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman al-Ajhuri Nur al-Din Abu al-Irshad. From his works: Sharh Alfiyyat Ibn Malik, Sharh al-Tahdhib lil-Taftazani fi al-Mantiq, born 967 AH, died 1066 AH. End. Hadiyyat al-Arifin (2/758).
Source pages p. 738

Commentary
This passage is a biographical appendix listing scholars mentioned in the commentary Imdad al-Fattah Sharh Nur al-Idah. It provides for each scholar: full name, school (if notable), year of birth and death, and major works, along with source references. Such glossaries are common in classical fiqh works to establish the authority of cited authors. The list includes scholars from various schools (Hanbali, Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanafi) and fields (fiqh, hadith, tafsir, grammar, Sufism). For students, this serves as a quick reference to contextualize the authorities relied upon in the commentary.

Key Terms
ابن قدامة (Ibn Qudamah): Abdullah ibn Ahmad, Hanbali scholar, author of al-Mughni.
أبو الليث السمرقندي (Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi): Nasr ibn Muhammad, a Hanafi faqih and mufassir who died 375 AH.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
10 min
The Hanafi Library: Understanding Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah and Source Hierarchy
Lists classical Hanafi texts with authors and death dates for reference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the six books of Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah and explain how the authority of a Hanafi work is assessed based on its type (foundational text, commentary, or fatwa collection) and author's death date.

Core Idea
Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah is the bedrock of the Hanafi school; later commentaries and fatwa collections derive from it but carry lower authority.

This passage is a selective bibliography of Hanafi works cited in the commentary. It lists foundational texts by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, such as al-Siyar al-Kabir and al-Ziyadat, as well as numerous commentaries (shuruh) and fatwa collections. Understanding the relative authority of these works is essential for proper istidlal (legal reasoning) and fatwa. In this lesson, you will focus on the concept of Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah—the six core books—and learn how to navigate the Hanafi literary tradition.

Guided Path
1
Locate the core definition
Find entry 121 in the list that defines 'Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah'. Identify the six books named: al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Mabsut (al-Asl), al-Ziyadat. Understand that these are the direct dictations of Imam Muhammad from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
These six books are the most authoritative in the Hanafi school; they are the primary source for fatwa when a ruling is found in them.
2
Categorize the entries by type
Scan the list and note which entries are original matns (e.g., al-Ziyadat, al-Siyar al-Saghir), which are commentaries (shuruh, e.g., Sharh al-Hidayah), and which are fatwa collections (al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya). This helps understand the genre and layer of authority.
Commentaries are secondary; they explain and sometimes expand on the matns. Fatwa collections are even later and may incorporate preferred positions (mufta bihi).
3
Analyze the chain of transmission
For a given commentary, trace back to the matn it explains. For example, Sharh al-Hidayah (entry 113) comments on al-Hidayah, which is itself a commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. This chain shows the layers of interpretation.
The closer a work is to the founding imams, the higher its authority generally.
4
Apply the hierarchy to a hypothetical fatwa scenario
If a ruling is reported in both al-Mabsut (a Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah text) and al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya, the ruling from al-Mabsut takes precedence unless a later tarjih (preference) exists. This illustrates the principle that Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah is the default authority.

الاختيار، وشرحه محمد بن إبراهيم بن أحمد السميديسي المدعو بالإمام وسماه فيض الغفار. ١٠٥- شرح مختصر الطحاوي فقد شرحه علي بن محمد الإسبيجابي المتوفى سنة (٤٥٤هـ)، وشرحه أحمد بن علي أبو بكر الجصاص المتوفي (۳۷۰هـ) وشرحه أحمد بن علي أبو بكر الوراق، وشرحه شمس الأئمة محمد بن أحمد السرخسي المتوفى سنة (٤٨٣هـ). ١٠٦- شرح المشارق للشيخ أكمل الدين محمد بن محمود البابرتي المتوفى سنة (٧٨٦هـ) وسماه تحفة الأبرار في شرح مشارق الأنوار. ۱۰۷- شرح المقدسي: للشيخ علي بن غانم المقدسي المتوفى سنة (١٠٠٤هـ). ١٠٨- شرح المنية لابن أمير حاج - المقدمة الغزنوية لأحمد بن محمد بن محمود بن سعد الغزنوي توفي بحلب سنة (٥٩٣هـ). ۱۳۳- غمز عيون البصائر على محاسن الأشباه والنظائر للإمام أحمد بن محمد الحنفي الحموي المتوفى سنة (١٠٩٨هـ). ١٣٤- الغيائية - الفتاوى الغياثية. ١٣٥ الفائق في غريب الحديث: للعلامة جار الله محمود بن عمر الزمخشري أبي القاسم المتوفى سنة (٥٣٨هـ). ١٣٦ الفتاوى الصغرى لعمر بن عبد العزيز بن مازه أبو م محمد حسام الدین المعروف بالصدر الشهيد رزق الشهادة سنة (٥٣٦هـ). ۱۳۷ - الفتاوى الظهيرية لظهير الدين أبي بكر محمد بن ا أحمد القاضي البخاري الحنفي المتوفى سنة (٦١٩هـ). ۱۳۸ - الفتاوى العتابية – جامع الفقه. ١٣٩- الفتاوى الغيائية للإمام داود بن يوسف الخطيب رتبه للسلطان غياث الدين تغلق.

al-Ikhtiyar, and its commentary by Muhammad ibn Ibrahim ibn Ahmad al-Samidisiy, called al-Imam, and he named it Fayd al-Ghaffar. 105- Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi: commented on by Ali ibn Muhammad al-Isbijabi, died 454 AH, and by Ahmad ibn Ali Abu Bakr al-Jassas, died 370 AH, and by Ahmad ibn Ali Abu Bakr al-Warraq, and by Shams al-A'imma Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Sarakhsi, died 483 AH. 106- Sharh al-Mashariq by Shaykh Akmal al-Din Muhammad ibn Mahmud al-Babarti, died 786 AH, and he called it Tuhfat al-Abrar fi Sharh Mashariq al-Anwar. 107- Sharh al-Maqdisi: by Shaykh Ali ibn Ghanim al-Maqdisi, died 1004 AH. 108- Sharh al-Munyah li Ibn Amir Haj - Hulbat al-Mujalli. 109- Sharh al-Munyah li Burhan al-Halabi Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Halabi, died 956 AH. 110- Sharh al-Muhadhdhab by Imam Yahya ibn Sharaf ibn Murri al-Nawawi Abu Zakariya, died 677 AH. 111- Sharh al-Mawahib - Mawahib al-Rahman - al-Burhan. 112- Sharh al-Nuqayah: al-Nuqayah has many commentaries, including by Shaykh Taqi al-Din Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Shumunni, died 872 AH, and by Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Bakr known as Ibn al-Ayni, died 893 AH, and by Mawlana Nur al-Din Ali ibn Sultan Muhammad al-Qari al-Harawi, died 1014 AH, and he called it Fath Bab al-Inayah. 113- Sharh al-Hidayah: al-Hidayah has many commentaries, including: al-Nihayah by al-Sanqaqi, died 710 AH; Ma'arij al-Dirayah by al-Kaki, died 749 AH; Nihayat al-Kifayah by al-Mahbubi, died 672 AH; al-Ghayah by al-Saruji, died 710 AH; Ghayat al-Bayan by al-Itqani, died 758 AH; Fath al-Qadir by al-Siwasi known as Ibn al-Humam, died 861 AH. 114- Shir'at al-Islam by Imam al-Wa'iz Rukn al-Islam Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr known as Imamzadeh al-Hanafi, died 573 AH. 115- Al-Shu'a' by Makhul ibn al-Fadl al-Nasafi, died 318 AH. 116- Al-Shu'ab - Shu'ab al-Iman - al-Jami' al-Musannaf fi Shu'ab al-Iman by Imam Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Husayn al-Bayhaqi, died 458 AH. 117- Al-Sihah by Imam Abu Nasr Isma'il ibn Hammad al-Jawhari al-Farabi, died 393 AH, first to adhere to authentic (hadith) limited to it, therefore he called his book al-Sihah. 118- Al-Sughra - al-Fatawa al-Sughra. 119- Salat al-Baqqali by Zayn al-Mashayikh Abu al-Fadl Muhammad ibn Abi al-Qasim al-Baqqali, died 562 AH. 120- Diya' al-Huloom fi Mukhtasar Shams al-Ulum by Muhammad ibn Nashwan ibn Sa'id al-Himyari. 121- Zahir al-Riwayah by Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, died 187 AH, and it consists of the books: al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Mabsut (al-Asl), al-Ziyadat. 122- Al-Zahiriyya - al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya. 123- Al-Itabiyya - al-Fatawa al-Itabiyya - Jami' al-Fiqh or (Jawami') al-Fiqh. 124- Umdat al-Nazir ala al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir by Imam al-Sayyid Muhammad ibn Abi al-Saud and his gloss compiled from the glosses of al-Hamawi, al-Bayri, and others. 125- Al-Inayah Sharh al-Hidayah by Shaykh Akmal al-Din Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Mahmud al-Babarti, who died in Egypt in 786 AH. 126- Al-Uyun - Uyun al-Masa'il: by Abu al-Layth Nasr ibn Muhammad al-Samarqandi, died 383 AH, and the commentary on Uyun al-Masa'il by Shaykh Ala' al-Din Muhammad ibn Abd al-Hamid al-Ismandi al-Samarqandi known as al-Ala' al-Alam, died 552 AH, and he called it (Hasar al-Masa'il wa Qasr al-Dala'il). 127- Uyun al-Madhahib by Imam Qiwam al-Din Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Kaki, died 749 AH. 128- Ghayat al-Bayan wa Nadirat al-Aqran by Shaykh al-Imam Amir Katib ibn Amir Umar al-Itqani al-Hanafi, died 758 AH, and it is a commentary on al-Hidayah. 129- Al-Ghayah Sharh al-Hidayah: famous as Ghayat al-Saruji by Shaykh Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Abd al-Ghani, died 710 AH, attributed to Saruj, a town in the land of Harran in the region of Jazirat Ibn Umar. 130- Ghurar al-Adhkar: Sharh Durar al-Bihar by Shaykh Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Mahmud al-Bukhari, died approximately 850 AH, lived in Syria and died there. 131- Al-Gharibayn: meaning Gharib al-Qur'an and al-Hadith by Abu Ubayd Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Harawi, died 401 AH. 132- Al-Ghaznawiyya - al-Muqaddimah al-Ghaznawiyya by Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Mahmud ibn Sa'd al-Ghaznawi, died in Aleppo in 593 AH. 133- Ghamz Uyun al-Basa'ir ala Mahasin al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir by Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Hanafi al-Hamawi, died 1098 AH. 134- Al-Ghiyathiyya - al-Fatawa al-Ghiyathiyya. 135- Al-Fa'iq fi Gharib al-Hadith: by Allama Jar Allah Mahmud ibn Umar al-Zamakhshari Abu al-Qasim, died 538 AH. 136- Al-Fatawa al-Sughra by Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz ibn Mazah Abu Muhammad Husam al-Din known as al-Sadr al-Shahid, martyred in 536 AH. 137- Al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya by Zahir al-Din Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Qadi al-Bukhari al-Hanafi, died 619 AH. 138- Al-Fatawa al-Itabiyya – Jami' al-Fiqh. 139- Al-Fatawa al-Ghiyathiyya by Imam Dawud ibn Yusuf al-Khatib, arranged for Sultan Ghiyath al-Din Tughluq.
Source pages p. 755

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography listing Hanafi works from entry 84 to 139, forming part of the source index for the commentary. It includes foundational texts like Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's al-Ziyadat and al-Siyar, as well as later commentaries such as al-Siraj al-Wahhaj on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Notably, entry 121 defines 'Zahir al-Riwayah' as the six core books of Imam Muhammad: al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Mabsut (al-Asl), and al-Ziyadat. The list also cites supercommentaries on al-Hidayah (entry 113) and fatwa collections like al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya. The author's method is to provide the full name of the work, its author, and the death date (in most cases), allowing the reader to assess the authority weight of each source. This index demonstrates the depth of the Hanafi tradition, spanning from the 2nd to the 10th centuries AH.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani: al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Mabsut (al-Asl), and al-Ziyadat. These are the most authoritative transmissions in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the six books of Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah according to entry 121?
A) Al-Mabsut
B) Al-Jami' al-Saghir
C) Sharh al-Hidayah
D) Al-Ziyadat

Key Takeaway
Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah, consisting of six core works by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, forms the highest authority in the Hanafi school; later commentaries and fatwa collections are derived and subordinate.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Navigating Imdad al-Fattah Using the Table of Contents
Listing chapter and section headings with page numbers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to navigate the structure of Imdad al-Fattah using its table of contents and identify which chapter covers a given Hanafi fiqh topic.

Core Idea
The table of contents is the map of the book – it shows the organization of Hanafi fiqh topics from purification to hajj.

This passage is the table of contents (فهرس الموضوعات) of Imdad al-Fattah Sharh Nur al-Idah. While not a legal text itself, it provides a structured overview of the entire book, listing all the chapters (abwab) and sections (fusul) with their page numbers. Mastering this map helps you locate any ruling quickly and understand the logical flow of Hanafi fiqh as presented by al-Shurunbulali and his commentator.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Major Books
Look for the main 'كتاب' headings: الطهارة, الصلاة, الصوم, الزكاة, الحج. These are the major divisions of the book.
The book covers the five pillars and related topics.
2
Recognize Chapters and Sections
Under each Book, find chapters (باب) and sections (فصل). For example, under 'كتاب الصلاة' you see 'باب الأذان', 'فصل في بيان واجب الصلاة', etc.
The hierarchy is Book > Chapter > Section.
3
Note Page Numbers
Each heading is followed by a page number (though some are garbled in OCR). Use these to turn directly to the discussion.
The page numbers may vary in different printings.
4
Observe the Sequence
The order reflects the typical fiqh curriculum: purification, then prayer, then fasting, then zakah, then hajj. Within each, topics follow logically (e.g., conditions before nullifiers).
This sequence aids in systematic study.
5
Use for Quick Reference
When you need a specific ruling (e.g., on sajdah al-sahw), scan the table for the relevant chapter title and page number.
This saves time and reinforces the overall structure.

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents (فهرس الموضوعات) of the book Imdād al-Fattāḥ Sharḥ Nūr al-Īḍāḥ. It provides a hierarchical outline of the entire work, starting with preliminary sections (introduction, biography of the author al-Shurunbulālī), then proceeding through the major books of fiqh: The Book of Purification (كتاب الطهارة), The Book of Prayer (كتاب الصلاة), The Book of Fasting (كتاب الصوم), The Book of Zakāh (كتاب الزكاة), and The Book of Ḥajj (كتاب الحج). Each book is divided into chapters (باب) and sections (فصل) with corresponding page numbers. The table of contents reveals the comprehensive range of topics covered, from the details of wuḍū’ and ghusl to prayer conditions, imamate, invalidators of prayer, funeral rites, fasting, i‘tikāf, zakāh, and the rituals of ḥajj. It also includes indices for Qur’anic verses, hadiths, biographies, and books. This table serves as a roadmap for the reader, showing the organization of rulings and discussions according to the Hanafi school. The page numbers, though sometimes garbled in the OCR, allow navigation within the printed work. The table of contents itself is not a legal text but a publisher’s addition to facilitate study of the original sharḥ.

Key Terms
فهرس الموضوعات (Fihris al-Mawḍū‘āt): Table of contents; a list of chapter and section headings with page numbers for navigation.
باب (Bāb): Chapter; a major subdivision within a book of fiqh.
فصل (Faṣl): Section; a subsection within a chapter covering a specific ruling or set of rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Book of Prayer

Key Takeaway
The table of contents of Imdad al-Fattah is an essential tool for navigating the comprehensive Hanafi fiqh discussions, providing a clear map of topics from purification to hajj.
